Published Time: 2003-10-24T05:49:18Z

Persecution of Muslims - Wikipedia

===============
Forced conversions of Muslims in Spain, 16th century, by [Edwin Long](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edwin_Long "Edwin Long") (1829–1891)

The **persecution of Muslims** has been recorded throughout the [history of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Islam "History of Islam"), beginning with its founding by [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") in the 7th century.

In the early days of [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") in [Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca "Mecca"), [pre-Islamic Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-Islamic_Arabia "Pre-Islamic Arabia"), the new [Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslims "Muslims") were frequently subjected to abuse and [persecution by the Meccans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_by_Meccans "Persecution of Muslims by Meccans"), known as the [Mushrikun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mushrikun "Mushrikun") in Islam, who were adherents to [polytheism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytheism "Polytheism"). In the contemporary period, Muslims have faced religious restrictions in some countries. Various incidents of Islamophobia have also occurred.

Medieval
--------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Medieval")]

### Early Islam

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Early Islam")]

Main article: [Persecution of Muslims by Meccans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_by_Meccans "Persecution of Muslims by Meccans")

In the early days of Islam in [Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca "Mecca"), the new Muslims were often subjected to abuse and persecution by the [pagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pagan "Pagan") Meccans (often called _Mushrikin_: the unbelievers or [polytheists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytheist "Polytheist")). Some were killed, such as [Sumayya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumayya "Sumayya"), the seventh convert to Islam, who was allegedly tortured first by [Amr ibn Hisham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amr_ibn_Hisham "Amr ibn Hisham").[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-1) Even the [Islamic prophet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_prophet "Islamic prophet")[Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_in_Islam "Muhammad in Islam") was subjected to such abuse; while he was praying near the [Kaaba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaaba "Kaaba"), [Uqba ibn Abu Mu'ayt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uqba_ibn_Abu_Mu%27ayt "Uqba ibn Abu Mu'ayt") threw the [entrails](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entrail "Entrail") of a sacrificed camel over him. Abu Lahab's wife [Umm Jamil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umm_Jamil "Umm Jamil") would regularly dump filth outside his door and placed thorns in the path to his house.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-2)[_[unreliable source?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable\_sources "Wikipedia:Reliable sources")_]

Accordingly, if free Muslims were attacked, slaves who converted were subjected to far worse. The master of the [Ethiopian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopia "Ethiopia")[Bilal ibn Rabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bilal_ibn_Rabah "Bilal ibn Rabah") (who would become the first [muezzin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muezzin "Muezzin")) would take him out into the desert in the boiling heat of midday and place a heavy rock on his chest, demanding that he forswear his religion and pray to the polytheists' gods and goddesses, until [Abu Bakr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Bakr "Abu Bakr") bought him and freed him.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-3)

### Crusades

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Crusades")]

Main article: [Crusades](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusades "Crusades")

The [First Crusade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Crusade "First Crusade") was launched in 1095 by [Pope Urban II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Urban_II "Pope Urban II"), with the stated goal of regaining control of the sacred city of [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") and the [Holy Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land") from the Muslims, who had captured them from the [Byzantines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") in 638. The [Fatimid Caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate "Fatimid Caliphate"), [Al Hakim of Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Hakim_bi-Amr_Allah "Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah"), known as the "mad Caliph"[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-4) destroyed the [Constantinian-era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantine_the_Great "Constantine the Great")[Church of the Holy Sepulcher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulcher "Church of the Holy Sepulcher") in 1009, as well as [other Christian churches and shrines in the Holy Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid_desecration_of_Jerusalem "Fatimid desecration of Jerusalem").

This event, in conjunction with the [killing of Germanic pilgrims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_German_Pilgrimage_of_1064%E2%80%9365 "Great German Pilgrimage of 1064–65") who were travelling from Byzantium to Jerusalem, raised the anger of Europe, and inspired Pope Urban II to call on all Catholic rulers, [knights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knight "Knight"), and noblemen to recapture the Holy Land from Muslim rule.

In part, it was also a response to the [Investiture Controversy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Investiture_Controversy "Investiture Controversy"), which was the most significant [conflict between secular and religious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state_(medieval) "Separation of church and state (medieval)") powers in [medieval Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Europe "Medieval Europe"). The controversy began as a dispute between the [Holy Roman Emperor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor "Holy Roman Emperor") and the [Gregorian Papacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pope_Gregory_VII "Pope Gregory VII") and gave rise to the political concept of [Christendom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christendom "Christendom") as a union of all peoples and sovereigns under the direction of the pope; as both sides tried to marshal public opinion in their favour, people became personally engaged in a dramatic religious controversy. Also of great significance in launching the crusade were the string of victories by the Seljuk Turks, which saw the end of Arab rule in Jerusalem.

[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Taking_of_Jerusalem_by_the_Crusaders%2C_15th_July_1099.jpg/250px-Taking_of_Jerusalem_by_the_Crusaders%2C_15th_July_1099.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Taking_of_Jerusalem_by_the_Crusaders,_15th_July_1099.jpg)

Capture of Jerusalem by the Crusaders in 1099

On 7 May 1099 the Crusaders reached [Jerusalem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"), which had been recaptured from the [Seljuks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seljuks "Seljuks") by the [Fatimids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid "Fatimid") of Egypt only a year before. On 15 July, the Crusaders were able to end the siege by breaking down sections of the walls and entering the city. Over the course of that afternoon, evening, and next morning, the Crusaders killed almost every inhabitant of Jerusalem, Muslims and Jews alike. Although many Muslims sought shelter atop the [Temple Mount](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount "Temple Mount") inside the [Al-Aqsa Mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qibli_Mosque "Qibli Mosque"), the Crusaders spared few lives. According to the anonymous _[Gesta Francorum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesta\_Francorum "Gesta Francorum")_, in what some believe to be one of the most valuable contemporary sources of the First Crusade, "...the slaughter was so great that our men waded in blood up to their ankles...."[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-5) (which is however rather a literary figure used multiple times in similar context than probable reality). According to Fulcher of Chartres: "Indeed, if you had been there you would have seen our feet coloured to our ankles with the blood of the slain. But what more shall I relate? None of them were left alive; neither women nor children were spared.".[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-6)[Tancred, Prince of Galilee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tancred,_Prince_of_Galilee "Tancred, Prince of Galilee") claimed the [Temple quarter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_in_Jerusalem "Temple in Jerusalem") for himself and offered protection to some of the Muslims there, but he was unable to prevent their deaths at the hands of his fellow Crusaders.

During the massacre committed in Jerusalem during the First Crusade, it was reported that the Crusaders "[circled] the screaming, flame-tortured humanity singing 'Christ We Adore Thee!' with their Crusader crosses held high".[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-7) Muslims were indiscriminately killed, and Jews who had taken refuge in their synagogue were killed when it was burnt down by the Crusaders.

### Southern Italy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Southern Italy")]

Further information: [History of Islam in southern Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Islam_in_southern_Italy "History of Islam in southern Italy"), [Emirate of Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Sicily "Emirate of Sicily"), [Muslim settlement of Lucera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_settlement_of_Lucera "Muslim settlement of Lucera"), and [Muslim conquest of Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Sicily "Muslim conquest of Sicily")

The island of [Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicily "Sicily") was conquered by the [Aghlabids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aghlabids "Aghlabids") in the 10th century after over a century of conflict, with the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") losing its final stronghold in 965.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-8) The [Normans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italo-Norman "Italo-Norman") conquered the last Arab Muslim stronghold by 1091.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-9) Subsequently, just as Muslims had previously imposed the [jizya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jizya "Jizya") tax on the non-Muslims of Sicily, the new rulers continued the practice and imposed the same tax now on the Muslims (locally spelled _gisia_). Another tax on levied them for a time was the _augustale_.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-10) Muslim rebellion broke out during the reign of [Tancred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tancred,_King_of_Sicily "Tancred, King of Sicily") as [King of Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Sicily "King of Sicily"). Lombard pogroms against Muslims started in the 1160s. Muslim and Christian communities in Sicily became increasingly geographically separated. The island's Muslim communities were mainly isolated beyond an internal frontier which divided the south-western half of the island from the Christian north-east. Sicilian Muslims were dependent on royal protection. When [King William the Good](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_II_of_Sicily "William II of Sicily") died in 1189, this royal protection was lifted, and the door was opened for widespread attacks against the island's Muslims. Tolerance towards Muslims ended with increasing Hohenstaufen control. Many oppressive measures, passed by [Frederick II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor"), were introduced in order to please the Popes to stop Islam from being practised in [Christendom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christendom "Christendom"): the result was in a rebellion of Sicily's Muslims. This triggered organized and systematic reprisals which marked the final chapter of Islam in Sicily. The rebellion abated, but direct papal pressure induced Frederick to mass transfer all his Muslim subjects deep into the Italian hinterland.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-11)[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-12)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-autogenerated2-13)[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-14)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] In 1224, [Frederick II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor") expelled all Muslims from the island transferring many to Lucera (_Lugêrah_, as it was known in Arabic) over the next two decades. In this controlled environment they could not challenge royal authority and they benefited the crown in taxes and military service. Their numbers eventually reached between 15,000 and 20,000, leading Lucera to be called _Lucaera Saracenorum_ because it represented the last stronghold of Islamic presence in Italy. During peacetime, Muslims in Lucera were predominantly farmers. They grew [durum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durum "Durum") wheat, [barley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barley "Barley"), [legumes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legume "Legume"), grapes, and other fruits. Muslims also kept bees for [honey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Honey "Honey").[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-15) The [Muslim settlement of Lucera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_settlement_of_Lucera "Muslim settlement of Lucera") was destroyed by [Charles II of Naples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_II_of_Naples "Charles II of Naples") with backing from the papacy. The Muslims were either massacred, forcibly converted, enslaved, or exiled. Their abandoned mosques were demolished, and churches were usually built in their place. The [Lucera Cathedral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucera_Cathedral "Lucera Cathedral") was built on the site of a mosque which was destroyed. The mosque was the last one still functioning in [medieval Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Italy "Medieval Italy") by that time.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-16)[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-17)[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-18)[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-19)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Some were exiled, with many finding asylum in [Albania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albania "Albania") across the [Adriatic Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea").[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-20)[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-21) Islam was no longer a major presence in the island by the 14th century.

The Aghlabids also conquered the island of [Malta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malta "Malta") at the same time during their invasion of Sicily.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-22) Per the [Al-Himyari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kitab_al-Rawd_al-Mitar "Kitab al-Rawd al-Mitar") the island was reduced to an uninhabited ruin due to the conquest. The place was later converted into a settlement by Muslims.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-23) The Normans conquered it at the same time as Sicily.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-24) The Normans however did not interfere in the matters of Muslims of the island and gave them a tributary status.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-25) Their conquest however led to the [Christianization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianization "Christianization") and [Latinization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latinization_(historical) "Latinization (historical)") of the island.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-26) An annual fine on the Christian community for killing of a Muslim was also repealed in the 12th century, signifying the degradation of the protection given to the Muslims.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-27) Most of the Maltese Muslims were deported by 1271.[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-28) All Maltese Muslims had converted to Christianity by the end of the 15th century and had to find ways to disguise their previous identities by Latinizing or adopting new surnames.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-29)

### Mongol invasions

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Mongol invasions")]

Main article: [Mongol invasions and conquests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests "Mongol invasions and conquests")

[Genghis Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genghis_Khan "Genghis Khan"), and the later [Yuan Emperors of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Yuan_emperors "List of Yuan emperors") imposed restrictive decrees which forbade Islamic practices like [halal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halal "Halal") butchering and forced Muslims to follow Mongol methods of butchering animals.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] As a result of these decrees, Muslims were forced to slaughter sheep in secret.[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-30) Genghis Khan referred to Muslims as "slaves", and he also commanded them to follow the Mongol method of eating rather than the halal one.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_][Circumcision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circumcision "Circumcision") was also forbidden.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-31)[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-32) Toward the end of [their rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuan_dynasty "Yuan dynasty"), the corruption of the Mongol court and the persecution of Muslims became so severe that Muslim generals joined [Han Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Han_Chinese "Han Chinese") in rebelling against the Mongols. The [Ming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ming_dynasty "Ming dynasty") founder Zhu Yuanzhang employed Muslim generals like [Lan Yu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lan_Yu_(general) "Lan Yu (general)") who rebelled against the Mongols and defeated them in combat. Some Muslim communities were named "kamsia", which, in [Hokkien](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hokkien "Hokkien") Chinese, means "thank you"; many Hui Muslims claim that their communities were named "kamsia" because the Han Chinese appreciated the important role which they had played in assisting them to overthrow the Mongols.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-33) The Muslims in the [Semu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semu "Semu") class also revolted against the Yuan dynasty in the [Ispah Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ispah_Rebellion "Ispah Rebellion") but the rebellion was crushed and the Muslims were massacred by the Yuan loyalist commander Chen Youding.

Further information: [Battle of Baghdad (1258)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(1258) "Battle of Baghdad (1258)") and [Mongol invasions of Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Syria "Mongol invasions of Syria")

[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Baghdad_old_Abbasid_Minaret.jpg/250px-Baghdad_old_Abbasid_Minaret.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baghdad_old_Abbasid_Minaret.jpg)

Minaret of Baghdad's [al-Khulafa Mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Khulafa_Mosque "Al-Khulafa Mosque") which was destroyed by the [Mongol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol "Mongol") ruler [Hulagu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulegu_Khan "Hulegu Khan") during the [1258 siege](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(1258) "Battle of Baghdad (1258)")

Following the brutal [Mongol invasion of Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Central_Asia "Mongol invasion of Central Asia") under [Genghis Khan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genghis_Khan "Genghis Khan"), and the [sack of Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Baghdad_(1258) "Battle of Baghdad (1258)") which occurred in 1258, the [Mongol Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire")'s rule extended across most Muslim lands in [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia"). The [Abbasid caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_caliphate "Abbasid caliphate") was destroyed and the [Islamic civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age") suffered much devastation, especially in [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia"), and [Tengriism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tengriism "Tengriism") and Buddhism replaced it as the official religions of the empire.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Brown-34) However, the Mongols attacked people for goods and riches, not because of their religion. Later, many Mongol khans and rulers such as those of the [Oljeitu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oljeitu "Oljeitu"), the [Ilkhanid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilkhanid "Ilkhanid"), and the [Golden Horde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Horde "Golden Horde") became Muslims along with their subjects. The Mongols made no real effort to replace Islam with any other religion, they just had the desire to plunder goods from anyone who did not submit to their rule, which was characteristic of Mongol warfare.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] During the [Yuan Dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yuan_Dynasty "Yuan Dynasty") which the Mongols founded in China, Muslim scientists were highly regarded and Muslim beliefs were also [respected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_during_the_Yuan_dynasty "Islam during the Yuan dynasty"). Regarding the Mongol attacks, the Muslim historian, [ibn al-Athir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_ibn_al-Athir "Ali ibn al-Athir") lamented:

> I shrank from giving a recital of these events on the account of their magnitude and abhorrence. Even now I come reluctant to the task, for who would deem it a light thing to sing the death song of Islam and the Muslims or find it easy to tell this tale? O that my mother had not given me birth![[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-35)

The detailed atrocities during the sack of Baghdad include:[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

*   The [Grand Library of Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Wisdom "House of Wisdom"), which contained countless precious historical documents and books on subjects that ranged from [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine") to [astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomy "Astronomy"), was destroyed. Survivors said that the waters of the [Tigris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris "Tigris") ran black with ink from the enormous quantities of books that were flung into the river.
*   Citizens attempted to flee, but they were intercepted by Mongol soldiers who killed them with abandon. Martin Sicker writes that close to 90,000 people may have died (Sicker 2000, p.111).[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] Other estimates go much higher. [Wassaf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wassaf "Wassaf") claims that the loss of life was several hundred thousand. Ian Frazier of _[The New Yorker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_New\_Yorker "The New Yorker")_ claims that estimates of the death toll range from 200,000 to one million.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-36)
*   The Mongols looted and destroyed mosques, palaces, libraries, and hospitals. Grand buildings which had taken generations to build were burned to the ground.
*   The [caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Musta%27sim "Al-Musta'sim") was captured and forced to watch as his citizens were murdered and his treasury was plundered. According to most accounts, the caliph was killed by trampling. The Mongols rolled the caliph up in a rug, and rode their horses over him, because they believed that the earth would be offended if it were ever touched by royal blood. All but one of his sons were killed, and the sole surviving son was sent to Mongolia.
*   [Hulagu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hulagu_Khan "Hulagu Khan") had to move his camp upwind from the city, due to the stench of decay that emanated from its ruins.

At the intervention of Hulagu's [Nestorian Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nestorianism "Nestorianism") wife, [Dokuz Khatun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dokuz_Khatun "Dokuz Khatun"), the city's Christian inhabitants were spared.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-37)[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-38) Hulagu offered the royal palace to the Nestorian [Catholicos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholicos "Catholicos")[Mar Makikha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mar_Makikha "Mar Makikha"), and he also ordered that a cathedral should be built for him.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-39) Ultimately, the seventh ruler of the Ilkhanate, [Mahmud Ghazan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahmud_Ghazan "Mahmud Ghazan"), converted from [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism") to Islam, and thus began the gradual decline of Tengrism and Buddhism in the region and its replacement by the renaissance of Islam. Later, three of the four principal Mongol khanates embraced Islam.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-40)

Muslim and Jewish paternal cousin marriage was banned by the Yuan dynasty which also forced Muslims to obey Mongol customs like levirate marriage.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-41)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-42)[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-43)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-44)[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-45)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-46)[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-47)[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-48)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-49)[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-50)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

### Iberian Peninsula

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Iberian Peninsula")]

Main articles: [Forced conversions of Muslims in Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forced_conversions_of_Muslims_in_Spain "Forced conversions of Muslims in Spain"), [Expulsion of the Moriscos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos "Expulsion of the Moriscos"), [Spanish Inquisition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition "Spanish Inquisition"), and [Islam in Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Spain "Islam in Spain")

See also: [Reconquista](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconquista "Reconquista") and [Morisco rebellions in Granada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morisco_rebellions_in_Granada "Morisco rebellions in Granada")

[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Itin_mertola.jpg/250px-Itin_mertola.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Itin_mertola.jpg)

Old Mosque in [Mértola](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M%C3%A9rtola "Mértola"), Portugal. Converted into a church.

[![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Image_of_Moor_%28Muslim%29_Being_Trampled_by_Conquistadors_Horse_-_Museo_Nacional_del_Virreinato_-_Tepotzotlan_-_Mexico.jpg/250px-Image_of_Moor_%28Muslim%29_Being_Trampled_by_Conquistadors_Horse_-_Museo_Nacional_del_Virreinato_-_Tepotzotlan_-_Mexico.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Image_of_Moor_(Muslim)_Being_Trampled_by_Conquistadors_Horse_-_Museo_Nacional_del_Virreinato_-_Tepotzotlan_-_Mexico.jpg)

A figure of a Moor being trampled by a [conquistador](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquistador "Conquistador")'s horse at the [National Museum of the Viceroyalty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museo_Nacional_del_Virreinato "Museo Nacional del Virreinato") in [Tepotzotlan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tepotzotlan "Tepotzotlan")

Arabs relying largely on [Berbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berber_people "Berber people")[conquered the Iberian Peninsula starting in 711](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania "Umayyad conquest of Hispania"), subduing the whole [Visigothic Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom "Visigothic Kingdom") by 725. The triumphant [Umayyads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate "Umayyad Caliphate") got conditional capitulations probably in most of the towns, so that they could get a compromise with the native population. This was not always so. For example, Mérida, Cordova, Toledo, or Narbonne were conquered by storm or after laying siege on them. The arrangement reached with the locals was based on respecting the laws and traditions used in each place, so that the _Goths_ (a legal concept, not an ethnic one, i.e. the communities ruled by the _[Forum Iudicum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forum\_Iudicum "Forum Iudicum")_) continued to be ruled on new conditions by their own tribunals and laws.[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-51) The Gothic Church remained in place and collaborated with the new masters. [Al-Andalus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") or Muslim ruled Iberian peninsula, was conquered by northern Christian kingdoms in 1492, as a result of their expansion taking place especially after the definite collapse of the [Caliphate of Cordova](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate_of_Cordova "Caliphate of Cordova") in 1031.

The coming of the Crusades (starting with the [massacre of Barbastro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_Barbastro "War of Barbastro")) and similarly entrenched positions on the northern African [Almoravids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty "Almoravid dynasty"), who took over al-Andalus as of 1086, added to the difficult coexistence between communities, including Muslims in Christian ruled territory, or the [Mozarabic rite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozarabic_rite "Mozarabic rite") Christians (quite different from those of the northern kingdoms), and further minority groups. The Almohads, a fanatic north African sect who later occupied al-Andalus, were the only Iberian Muslim rulers to demand conversion, exile, or death from the Christians and Jews.[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-52)

[![Image 17](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg/250px-Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg)

[Expulsion of the Moriscos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos "Expulsion of the Moriscos") from Valencia

During the expansion south of the northern Christian kingdoms, depending on the local capitulations, local Muslims were allowed to remain ([Mudéjars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar "Mudéjar")) with extreme restrictions, while some were peacefully converted to the Christian faith. After the [conquest of Granada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conquest_of_Granada "Conquest of Granada"), all the Spanish Muslims were under Christian rule. The new acquired population spoke Arabic or [Mozarabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozarabic_language "Mozarabic language"), and the campaigns to convert them were unsuccessful. Legislation was gradually introduced to remove Islam, culminating with the Muslims being forced to convert to Catholicism by the [Spanish Inquisition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition "Spanish Inquisition"). They were known as [Moriscos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morisco "Morisco") and considered [New Christians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Christian "New Christian"). Further laws were introduced, as on 25 May 1566, stipulating that they "had to abandon the use of Arabic, change their costumes, that their doors must remain open every Friday, and other feast days, and that their baths, public and private, to be torn down."[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-53) The reason doors were to be left open so as to determine whether they secretly observed any Islamic festivals.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-54) King [Philip II of Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain "Philip II of Spain") ordered the destruction of all public baths on the grounds of them being relics of infidelity, notorious for their use by Muslims performing their purification rites.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-55)[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-56) The possession of books or papers in Arabic was near concrete proof of disobedience with severe reprisals and penalties.[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-57) On 1 January 1568, Christian priests were ordered to take all Morisco children between the ages of three and fifteen, and place them in schools, where they were forced to learn Castillian and Christian doctrine.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-58) All these laws and measures required force to be implemented, and from much earlier.

Between 1609 and 1614 the Moriscos were expelled from Spain.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-59) They were to depart 'under the pain of death and confiscation, without trial or sentence ... to take with them no money, bullion, jewels, or bills of exchange ... just what they could carry.'[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-60)

All in all, it is estimated that hundreds of thousands of Muslims (as well as Jews and Protestants) were forcibly converted to Catholicism, expelled, or tortured to death during the Inquisition.[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-61)

### Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth")]

Main articles: [Lipka Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipka_Tatars "Lipka Tatars") and [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania")

See also: [Lipka Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipka_Rebellion "Lipka Rebellion")

The [Lipka Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipka_Tatars "Lipka Tatars"), also known as Polish Tatars or Lithuanian Tatars, were a community of Tatar Muslims who migrated into the [Grand Duchy of Lithuania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania "Grand Duchy of Lithuania") and became [Polonized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polonized "Polonized").

The [Counter-Reformation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-Reformation "Counter-Reformation") of the [Catholic Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") in the [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth") led to persecution of Muslims, [Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews_in_Poland "Jews in Poland"), and [Orthodox Christians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox "Eastern Orthodox"). The ways the Muslims were persecuted included banning the repair of old mosques and preventing new ones from being constructed, banning [serfdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serfdom "Serfdom") of Christians under Muslims, banning marriage of Christian females to Muslims, putting limitations on property ownership among Tatars and the [Polish–Ottoman Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Ottoman_Wars "Polish–Ottoman Wars") fed into the discriminatory atmosphere against them and led to anti-Islamic writings and attacks.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Akiner2009-62)

### Sikh Khalsa and Sikh Empire

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Sikh Khalsa and Sikh Empire")]

[Misr Diwan Chand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Misr_Diwan_Chand "Misr Diwan Chand") became the first Hindu governor of Kashmir under Singh and enacted dozens of anti-Muslim laws. He raised the tax levels of Muslim subjects, demolished the Jamia Masjid of [Srinagar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srinagar "Srinagar") and prohibited cow slaughter. The punishment for cow slaughter was the death penalty without any exception.[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-63)[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-64)[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-65)[Shah Shuja Durrani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah_Shuja_Durrani "Shah Shuja Durrani"), the grandson of [Ahmad Shah Durrani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Durrani "Ahmad Shah Durrani"), wanted to implement similar anti-cow slaughter policies in the [Emirate of Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Afghanistan "Emirate of Afghanistan") and with help from Singh and the [East India Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_India_Company "East India Company") regained the Afghan throne and imposed a ban on cow slaughter in Kabul.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-66)

[Sayyid Ahmed Barelvi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syed_Ahmad_Barelvi "Syed Ahmad Barelvi") declared war against Maharaja Ranjit Singh and recruited many Muslims from madrassas. However the Yousufzai and Muhammadzai Khawaneen did not like his egalitarian ideals and betrayed Sayyid Ahmed Shahid and his army at the battle of Balakot and supported the Sikh Army in the Battle of Balakote in 1831, and Barelvi's head was severed by the Sikh General [Hari Singh Nalwa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hari_Singh_Nalwa "Hari Singh Nalwa").[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-67)[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-68)

Muslims still revered Sayyid Ahmed, however he was defeated and killed in the battle by Sikh Army which was commanded by [Hari Singh Nalwa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hari_Singh_Nalwa "Hari Singh Nalwa") and [Gulab Singh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulab_Singh "Gulab Singh").[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-69) Raja Aggar Khan of [Rajouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajouri "Rajouri") was defeated, humiliated by the Sikh Army commander Gulab Singh and was brought to Lahore where he was beheaded by Gulab Singh of Jammu. Raja Sultan Khan of [Bhimber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhimber "Bhimber") also met the same fate when he was defeated and captured by the Dogra ruler Gulab Singh and brought to [Jammu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu "Jammu") where he was imprisoned. Raja Sultan Khan later died in prison.[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-70)

### Dutch East India Company

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Dutch East India Company")]

The Dutch East India Company and Japanese samurai they hired as mercenaries committed genocide against Muslim Bandanese on the Banda islands, quartering in their mosques, humiliating their women and beheading their orang kaya in the [conquest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_conquest_of_the_Banda_Islands "Dutch conquest of the Banda Islands") of the [Banda Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governorate_of_the_Banda_Islands "Governorate of the Banda Islands").[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-71)[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-72)[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-73)[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-74)[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-75)

Modern era
----------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Modern era")]

### Americas

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Americas")]

See also: [Islam in the Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_Americas "Islam in the Americas")

In his book _God's Shadow_, historian [Alan Mikhail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alan_Mikhail "Alan Mikhail") posits that the 1492 [voyage to the Americas by Columbus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus "Voyages of Christopher Columbus") was driven in part by [Islamophobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobia "Islamophobia") views. European Christians arriving in the Americas perceived local customs as being Islamic and used this as a rationale for genociding the indigenous people.[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-76) Muslims who were brought to the region as slaves, though mistreated, found several ways to hold onto aspects of their faith.[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-77)

### Bulgaria

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Bulgaria")]

Main articles: [Islam in Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Bulgaria "Islam in Bulgaria"), [Turks in Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turks_in_Bulgaria "Turks in Bulgaria"), [Bulgarian Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian_Muslims "Bulgarian Muslims"), and [Pomak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pomak "Pomak")

[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Distribution_Clothing_Turkish_Refugees_1877.jpg/250px-Distribution_Clothing_Turkish_Refugees_1877.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Distribution_Clothing_Turkish_Refugees_1877.jpg)

War distribution of clothing to [Bulgarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian_people "Bulgarian people") Muslim refugees in Shumla from _The Illustrated London News_, 17 November 1877

Half a million Muslims succeeded in reaching Ottoman controlled lands and 672,215 of them were reported to have remained after the war. Approximately a quarter of a million of them perished as a result of massacres, cold, disease, and other harsh conditions.[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-78) According to Aubaret, the French Consul in [Ruse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruse,_Bulgaria "Ruse, Bulgaria") in 1876, in the [Danube Vilayet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danube_Vilayet "Danube Vilayet") which also included Northern Dobruja in today's Romania, as well as a substantial portion of territory in today's southern Serbia, there were 1,120,000 Muslims and 1,233,500 non-Muslims of whom 1,150,000 were Bulgarian. Between 1876 and 1878, through massacres, epidemics, hunger, and war, a large portion of the Turkish population vanished.[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-79) In [1950-1951 around 155,000 left Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exodus_of_Turks_from_Bulgaria_(1950-1951) "Exodus of Turks from Bulgaria (1950-1951)") as a result of Islamophobia and Anti-Turkish sentiment.

### Cambodia

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Cambodia")]

The [Cham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chams "Chams") Muslims experienced serious purges in which as much as half of their community's entire population was exterminated by authoritarian communists in Cambodia during the 1970s as part of the [Cambodian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian_genocide "Cambodian genocide").[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-80) About half a million Muslims were killed. According to Cham sources, 132 mosques were destroyed by the [Khmer Rouge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khmer_Rouge "Khmer Rouge")[regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea "Democratic Kampuchea"). Only 20 of the 113 most prominent Cham clerics in Cambodia survived the rule of the Khmer Rouge.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-81)

### China

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: China")]

Further information: [Persecution of Uyghurs in China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Uyghurs_in_China "Persecution of Uyghurs in China") and [Xinjiang internment camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang_internment_camps "Xinjiang internment camps")

See also: [Dungan Revolt (1862–1877)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dungan_Revolt_(1862%E2%80%931877) "Dungan Revolt (1862–1877)"), [Dungan revolt (1895–1896)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dungan_revolt_(1895%E2%80%931896) "Dungan revolt (1895–1896)"), [Ghulja incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghulja_incident "Ghulja incident"), [July 2009 Ürümqi riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots "July 2009 Ürümqi riots"), and [Panthay Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panthay_Rebellion "Panthay Rebellion")

[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Capture_of_the_Provincial_Capital_Dali%2C_Yunnan.jpg/250px-Capture_of_the_Provincial_Capital_Dali%2C_Yunnan.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Capture_of_the_Provincial_Capital_Dali,_Yunnan.jpg)

Capture of [Dali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dali_City "Dali City"), the capital of the Pingnan Sultanate in [Yunnan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yunnan "Yunnan"), from the set _Victory over the Muslims_

The Dungan revolt erupted due to infighting between Muslim Sufi sects, the Khafiya and the Jahariyya, and the [Gedimu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gedimu "Gedimu"). When the rebellion failed, mass-immigration of the [Dungan people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dungan_people "Dungan people") into [Imperial Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire"), [Kazakhstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhstan "Kazakhstan"), and [Kyrgyzstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyrgyzstan "Kyrgyzstan") ensued. Before the war, the population of Shaanxi province totalled approximately 13 million inhabitants, at least 1,750,000 of whom were Dungan (Hui). After the war, the population dropped to 7 million; at least 150,000 fled. But once-flourishing Chinese Muslim communities fell 93% in the revolt in Shaanxi province. Between 1648 and 1878, around twelve million [Hui](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hui_people "Hui people") and Han Chinese were killed in ten unsuccessful uprisings.[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-82)[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-83)

The [Ush rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ush_rebellion&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ush rebellion (page does not exist)") in 1765 by [Uyghur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghurs "Uyghurs") Muslims against the [Manchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchu_people "Manchu people") of the [Qing dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qing_dynasty "Qing dynasty") occurred after Uyghur women were gang raped by the servants and son of Manchu official Su-cheng.[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-84)[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-85)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-86) It was said that _Ush Muslims had long wanted to sleep on [Sucheng and son's] hides and eat their flesh._ because of the rape of Uyghur Muslim women for months by the Manchu official Sucheng and his son.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Millward-87) The Manchu Emperor ordered that the Uyghur rebel town be massacred, the Qing forces enslaved all the Uyghur children and women and slaughtered the Uyghur men.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Millward-87) Manchu soldiers and Manchu officials regularly having sex with or raping Uyghur women caused massive hatred and anger by Uyghur Muslims to Manchu rule. The [invasion by Jahangir Khoja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%80f%C4%81q%C4%AB_Khoja_Holy_War "Āfāqī Khoja Holy War") was preceded by another Manchu official, Binjing who raped a Muslim daughter of the Kokan aqsaqal from 1818 to 1820. The Qing sought to cover up the rape of Uyghur women by Manchus to prevent anger against their rule from spreading among the Uyghurs.[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-88)

The Manchu official Shuxing'a started an anti-Muslim massacre which led to the [Panthay Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panthay_Rebellion "Panthay Rebellion"). Shuxing'a developed a deep hatred of Muslims after an incident where he was stripped naked and nearly lynched by a mob of Muslims. He ordered several Hui Muslim rebels to be slowly sliced to death.[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-89)[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-90)

The revolts were harshly suppressed by the Manchu government in a manner that amounts to genocide.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-91)[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-92)[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-93)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-94) Approximately a million people in the [Panthay Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panthay_Rebellion "Panthay Rebellion") were killed,[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-95)[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-chineseciv-96) and several million in the Dungan revolt[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-chineseciv-96) as a "[washing off](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") the Muslims"(洗回 (xi Hui)) policy had been long advocated by officials in the [Manchu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qing_dynasty "Qing dynasty") government.[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-97) Many Muslim generals like [Ma Zhanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Zhanao "Ma Zhanao"), [Ma Anliang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Anliang "Ma Anliang"), [Ma Qianling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Qianling "Ma Qianling"), [Dong Fuxiang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dong_Fuxiang "Dong Fuxiang"), [Ma Haiyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Haiyan "Ma Haiyan"), and [Ma Julung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Rulong_(Qing_general) "Ma Rulong (Qing general)") helped the Qing dynasty defeat the rebel Muslims, and were rewarded, and their followers were spared from the genocide. The Han Chinese Qing general [Zuo Zongtang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zuo_Zongtang "Zuo Zongtang") even relocated the Han from the suburbs [Hezhou](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hezhou "Hezhou") when the Muslims there surrendered as a reward so that Hezhou (now [Linxia Hui Autonomous Prefecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linxia_Hui_Autonomous_Prefecture "Linxia Hui Autonomous Prefecture")) is still heavily Muslim to this day and is the most important city for Hui Muslims in China. The Muslims were granted amnesty and allowed to live as long as they stayed outside the city.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-98) Some of the Muslims who fought, like General Dong, did not do it because they were Muslim, rather, like many other generals, they gathered bands of followers and fought at will.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-99)[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-100)

[![Image 20: Street demonstration with banners, passing an official building](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg/250px-Uyghur_protest_Berlin%2C_July_2009_3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Uyghur_protest_Berlin,_July_2009_3.jpg)

Demonstration in Berlin for Uyghur human rights

Zuo Zongtang generally massacred New Teaching Jahriyya rebels, even if they surrendered, but spared Old Teaching Khafiya and Sunni Gedimu rebels. Ma Hualong belonged to the New Teaching school of thought, and Zuo executed him, while Hui generals belonging to the Old Teaching clique such as Ma Qianling, Ma Zhan'ao, and Ma Anliang were granted amnesty and even promoted in the Qing military. Moreover, an army of Han Chinese rebels led by [Dong Fuxiang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dong_Fuxiang "Dong Fuxiang") surrendered and joined Zuo Zongtang.[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Garnaut-101) General Zuo accepted the surrender of Hui people belonging to the Old Teaching school, provided they surrendered large amounts of military equipment and supplies, and accepted relocation. He refused to accept the surrender of New Teaching Muslims who still believed in its tenets, since the Qing classified them as a dangerous heterodox cult, similar to the [White Lotus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Lotus_Societies "White Lotus Societies") Buddhists.[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-102)

The Qing authorities decreed that the Hui rebels who had taken part in violent attacks were merely heretics and not representative of the entire Hui population, just as the heretical White Lotus did not represent all Buddhists.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-103) Qing authorities decreed that there were two different Muslim sects, the "old" religion and "new" religion. The new were heretics and deviated from Islam in the same way that the White Lotus deviated from Buddhism and Daoism, and stated its intention to inform the Hui community that it was aware that the original Islamic religion was one united sect before the advent of new "heretics", saying they would separate Muslim rebels by which sect they belonged to.[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-104) Zuo also stated that he would accept the surrender of New Teaching Muslims who admitted that they were deceived, radicalized, and misled by its doctrines. Zuo excluded khalifas and mullas from the surrender.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-105)

During the [Cultural Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_Revolution "Cultural Revolution"), mosques along with other religious buildings were often defaced, destroyed, or closed and copies of the [Quran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran") were destroyed and cemeteries by the [Red Guards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Guards_(China) "Red Guards (China)").[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-106) During that time, the government also constantly accused Muslims and other religious groups of holding "superstitious beliefs" and promoting "[anti-socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-socialist "Anti-socialist") trends".[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-107) The government began to relax its policies toward Muslims in 1978, and supported worship and rituals. Today, Islam is experiencing a modest revival and there are now[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-108)[many mosques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mosques_in_China "List of mosques in China") in China. There has been an upsurge in Islamic expression and many nationwide Islamic associations have been organized to co-ordinate inter-ethnic activities among Muslims.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-109)

However, restrictions have been imposed on Uyghur Islamic practices because the Chinese government has attempted to link Islamic beliefs with terrorist activities since 2001. Numerous events have led the Chinese government to crack down on most displays of Islamic piety among Uyghurs, including the wearing of veils and long beards. The [Ghulja Incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghulja_Incident "Ghulja Incident") and the [July 2009 Ürümqi riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/July_2009_%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi_riots "July 2009 Ürümqi riots") were both caused by abusive treatment of Uyghur Muslims within Chinese society, and they resulted in even more extreme government crackdowns. While Hui Muslims are seen as being relatively docile, Uyghurs are stereotyped as [Islamists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamism "Islamism") and punished more severely for crimes than Hui are. In 1989, China's government banned a book which was titled _Xing Fengsu_ ("Sexual Customs") and placed its authors under arrest after Uyghurs and Hui Muslims protested against its publication in Lanzhou and Beijing because it insulted Islam.[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Beijing_Review,_Volume_32_1989-110)[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Gladney_1991-111)[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Schein_2000-112)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Gladney_2004-113)[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Bulag_2010-114)[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Gladney_2005-115)[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Gladney_2013-116)[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Sautman_2000-117)[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Gladney_1996-118)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Hui Muslims who vandalized property during the protests against the book's publication were not punished but Uyghur protestors were imprisoned.[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-books.google.com-119)

### Fascist Italy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Fascist Italy")]

Main articles: [Libyan genocide (1929–1934)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libyan_genocide_(1929%E2%80%931934) "Libyan genocide (1929–1934)") and [Italian concentration camps in Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_concentration_camps_in_Libya "Italian concentration camps in Libya")

[![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Al-Magroon_Concentration_Camp.jpg/250px-Al-Magroon_Concentration_Camp.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Al-Magroon_Concentration_Camp.jpg)

Ten thousand inmates were kept at the concentration camp in [El Agheila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Agheila "El Agheila").

The [Libyan genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libyan_genocide_(1929%E2%80%931934) "Libyan genocide (1929–1934)") was the systematic destruction of the indigenous Libyan [Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs "Arabs") people and culture in [Italian Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_colonization_of_Libya "Italian colonization of Libya") by the [Italian colonial authorities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Empire "Italian Empire") from 1911 to 1943, using the wider definition of [genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide"), where an estimated 250,000-750,000 Libyans died as a result of colonial-related causes.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:6-120)[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-121) The most severe and frequent episodes of Italian atrocities against the locals came during the conflict between Italy and the indigenous rebels of the [Senussi Order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senussi "Senussi") that lasted from 1923 until 1932, when the principal Senussi leader, [Omar Mukhtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omar_Mukhtar "Omar Mukhtar"), was captured and executed. Italy committed major [war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_crime "War crime") during the conflict; including the use of [chemical weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemical_weapon "Chemical weapon"), episodes of refusing to take prisoners of war and instead executing surrendering combatants, and mass executions of civilians.[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-122)[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-123)[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-124) During this period, an estimated 83,000-125,000 Libyans were massacred or died in Italian concentration camps.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-125)[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:6-120)

### French Algeria

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: French Algeria")]

Main articles: [French Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Algeria "French Algeria"), [Pacification of Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacification_of_Algeria "Pacification of Algeria"), [Algerian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "Algerian War"), and [Torture during the Algerian War of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torture_during_the_Algerian_War_of_Independence "Torture during the Algerian War of Independence")

See also: [Indigénat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indig%C3%A9nat "Indigénat") and [Sétif and Guelma massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A9tif_and_Guelma_massacre "Sétif and Guelma massacre")

Some governments and scholars have called the [French conquest of Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_conquest_of_Algeria "French conquest of Algeria") a genocide. [Ben Kiernan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ben_Kiernan "Ben Kiernan"), an Australian expert on the [Cambodian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cambodian_genocide "Cambodian genocide"), wrote in _[Blood and Soil: A World History of Genocide and Extermination from Sparta to Darfur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood\_and\_Soil\_(book) "Blood and Soil (book)")_ on the French conquest of Algeria:[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-126)

> By 1875, the French conquest was complete. The war had killed approximately 825,000 indigenous Algerians since 1830. A long shadow of genocidal hatred persisted, provoking a French author to protest in 1882 that in Algeria, "we hear it repeated every day that we must expel the native and if necessary destroy him." As a French statistical journal urged five years later, "the system of extermination must give way to a policy of penetration."

During the French conquest from 1830 to 1875, the native Algerian population fell by up to one-third due to war, massacres, famine and disease. Between 500,000 and 1,000,000 Algerians, out of a total of 3 million, were killed.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-127)[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-128)[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Kiernan2007-129) Atrocities committed by the French during this period include wholesale massacres of civilians, [scorched earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorched_earth "Scorched earth") tactics, destroying mosques and converting them to Catholic churches, burying people alive, and French horse units throwing boiling water on Algerians perceived to be resisting in any way.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-130)[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-131)[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-132)[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-133)[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0-134)[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-scoear-135)[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-tribekil-136)[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-137)[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-138)[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0a-139)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:1-140) During the period of 1954-1962, in the [Algerian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "Algerian War"), an estimated 400,000-1.5 million Algerians lost their lives.[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-141)[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-142)[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-143) Atrocities committed by French troops include massacres of civilians, (perhaps most infamously the [Setif and Guelma massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Setif_and_Guelma_massacre "Setif and Guelma massacre"), where 3,000 to 45,000 Algerian civilians were massacred by French troops and [Pied-Noir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pied-Noir "Pied-Noir") vigilante mobs), rape, torture by electric shock, burning and beating, burial alive, [death flights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_flights "Death flights"), sexual assaults, and the use of napalm to indiscriminately burn villages and towns.[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-144)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-145)[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-146)[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-147)[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-148)[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-149) The French sent over 2 million Algerians to concentration camps, where they were kept in deplorable, prison-like conditions, and destroyed over 8,000 villages during the war.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-150)[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-151)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-152) In 2018, France admitted torture was routine and systematic during the Algerian war of independence.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-153)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-154) Algeria became the prototype for a pattern of French colonial rule which has been described as "quasi-[apartheid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid")".[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-155)[Napoleon III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon_III "Napoleon III") oversaw an 1865 decree that allowed Arab and [Berber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berber_people "Berber people") Algerians to request French citizenship – but only if they "renounced their Muslim religion and culture":[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-156) by 1913, only 1,557 Muslims had been granted French citizenship.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-157) Despite periodic attempts at partial reform, the situation of the _[Code de l'indigénat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code\_de\_l%27indig%C3%A9nat "Code de l'indigénat")_ persisted until the [French Fourth Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic "French Fourth Republic"), which began in 1946, but although Muslim Algerians were accorded the rights of citizenship, the system of discrimination was maintained in more informal ways.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-158) This "internal system of apartheid" met with considerable resistance from the Muslims affected by it, and is cited as one of the causes of the [1954 insurrection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_War "Algerian War").[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Wall-159)

In response to France's recognition of [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide"), Turkey accused France of committing genocide against 15% of Algeria's population.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-160)[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-161) In October 2021, the office of Algerian president [Abdelmadjid Tebboune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune "Abdelmadjid Tebboune") stated that 5.6 million Algerians had died during the country’s 132 years under French colonial rule, while historian Mohammed Al-Amin estimated that the total Algerian death toll could be as high as 10 million.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-162)[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-163)[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-164)

It is estimated that between 27,000 and 60,000 Algerians were affected by radiation from French nuclear weapons tests in the [Algerian Desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_Desert "Algerian Desert"), with thousands having long-lasting health effects and deformities due to radiation exposure.[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-165)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-166)[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-167)[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-168)

### French Morocco

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: French Morocco")]

Generally speaking, French colonialism in Morocco was highly discriminatory against indigenous Moroccans and was detrimental to the Moroccan economy. Native Moroccans were treated as second class citizens and discriminated against in nearly all aspects of life. Additionally, land in Morocco was far more expensive for Moroccans than for French settlers.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-169) Various historians have estimated that around 100,000 Moroccans were killed during the [French conquest of Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_conquest_of_Morocco "French conquest of Morocco") between 1907 and 1934. Around 8,000 French soldiers and 12,000 native Moroccans soldiers in the French army were also killed.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:8-170)[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-171) Historian Daniel Rivet adds that the tally would be significantly higher if including the enormous suffering of the Riffian tribes during the [Rif War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rif_War "Rif War") between 1921 and 1926.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:8-170)

### Imperial Japan

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Imperial Japan")]

Main articles: [Rakhine State massacre in 1942](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rakhine_State_massacre_in_1942 "Rakhine State massacre in 1942") and [Japanese occupation of the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_the_Philippines "Japanese occupation of the Philippines")

Imperial Japanese forces slaughtered, raped, and tortured [Rohingya Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rohingya_people "Rohingya people") in a massacre in 1942 and expelled hundreds of thousands of Rohingya into Bengal in British India. The Japanese committed countless acts of rape, murder, and torture against thousands of Rohingyas.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-172) During this period, some 220,000 Rohingyas are believed to have crossed the border into [Bengal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal "Bengal"), then part of British India, to escape the violence.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-173)[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-174) Defeated, 40,000 Rohingyas eventually fled to Chittagong after repeated massacres by the Burmese and Japanese forces.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-175)

Japanese forces also carried out massacres, torture, and atrocities on Muslim [Moro people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_people "Moro people") in [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao"), and [Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulu "Sulu"). A former Japanese Imperial Navy medic, [Akira Makino](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akira_Makino "Akira Makino"), admitted to carrying out dissections on Moro civilians while they were still alive.[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-176)[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-177)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-178)[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-179)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

[Panglong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panlong_Subtownship "Panlong Subtownship"), a Chinese Muslim town in [British Burma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_rule_in_Burma "British rule in Burma"), was entirely destroyed by the Japanese invaders in the [Japanese invasion of Burma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Burma "Japanese invasion of Burma").[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-180) The Hui Muslim Ma Guanggui became the leader of the Hui Panglong self-defense guard created by Su who was sent by the [Kuomintang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuomintang "Kuomintang") government of the [Republic of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%931949) "Republic of China (1912–1949)") to fight against the Japanese invasion of Panglong in 1942. The Japanese destroyed Panglong, burning it and driving out the over 200 Hui households out as refugees. Yunnan and Kokang received Hui refugees from Panglong driven out by the Japanese. One of Ma Guanggui's nephews was Ma Yeye, a son of Ma Guanghua and he narrated the history of Panglang including the Japanese attack.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-181) An account of the Japanese attack on the Hui in Panglong was written and published in 1998 by a Hui from Panglong called "Panglong Booklet".[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-182) The Japanese attack in Burma caused the Hui Mu family to seek refuge in Panglong but they were driven out again to Yunnan from Panglong when the Japanese attacked Panglong.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-183)

[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Horrible_death%2C_Nanking_Massacre.jpg/250px-Horrible_death%2C_Nanking_Massacre.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Horrible_death,_Nanking_Massacre.jpg)

Dead bodies of the Chinese Hui Muslim Ha family who were slaughtered and raped by the Japanese in Nanjing. The photo comes from Case 5 of [John Magee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Magee_(missionary) "John Magee (missionary)")'s film. On 13 December 1937, about 30 Japanese soldiers murdered all but two of 11 Chinese Hui Muslims from the Ha family in the house at No. 5 Xinlukou. A woman and her two teenaged daughters were raped, and Japanese soldiers rammed a bottle and a cane into her vagina. An eight-year-old girl was stabbed, but she and her younger sister survived. They were found alive two weeks after the killings by the elderly woman shown in the photo. Bodies of the victims can also be seen in the photo.[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-184)[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-185)

[The Hui Muslim county of Dachang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dachang_Hui_Autonomous_County "Dachang Hui Autonomous County") was subjected to slaughter by the Japanese.[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-186)

During the [Second Sino-Japanese war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_war "Second Sino-Japanese war") the Japanese followed what has been referred to as a "killing policy" and destroyed many mosques. According to Wan Lei, "Statistics showed that the Japanese destroyed 220 mosques and killed countless Hui people by April 1941." After the [Rape of Nanking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rape_of_Nanking "Rape of Nanking") mosques in Nanjing were found to be filled with dead bodies. They also followed a policy of economic oppression which involved the destruction of mosques and Hui communities and made many Hui jobless and homeless. Another policy was one of deliberate humiliation. This included soldiers smearing mosques with pork fat, forcing Hui to butcher pigs to feed the soldiers, and forcing girls to supposedly train as geishas and singers but in fact made them serve as sex slaves. Hui cemeteries were destroyed for military reasons.[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-187) Many Hui [fought in the war against Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Muslims_in_the_Second_Sino-Japanese_war "Chinese Muslims in the Second Sino-Japanese war").
