The Japanese brought Indonesian Javanese girls to British Borneo as comfort women to be raped by Japanese officers at the Ridge road school and Basel Mission Church, and the Telecommunication Center Station (former rectory of the All Saints Church) in Kota Kinabalu as well as ones in Balikpapan and Beaufort. Japanese soldiers raped Indonesian women and Dutch women in the Netherlands East Indies. They got infected with STDs.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-188)[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-189)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-190)

Sukarno prostituted Indonesian girls from ethnic groups like Minangkabau to the Japanese.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-191)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-192)[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-193)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-194)[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-195)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

The Japanese massacred Hui Muslims in their mosques in Nanjing and destroyed Hui mosques in other parts of China.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-196) Shen Xi’en and his father Shen Decheng witnessed the corpses of Hui Muslims slaughtered by the Japanese in Nanjing, when he was asked by Hui people to help bury their relatives. The Hui security maintenance leader Sun Shurong and Hui Imams Zhang Zihui, Ma Zihe, Ge Changfa, Wang Shouren, Ma Changfa were involved in collecting Hui corpses and burying them after the Nanjing massacre. The Ji'e lane Mosque caretaker father Zhang was in his 60s when killed by the Japanese and his decomposing corpse was the first to be washed in accordance with Islamic customs and buried. They buried the Hui corpses in Jiuhua mountain, Dongguashi, Hongtu Bridge (where Guangzhou road is now located), Wutai mountain, Donguashi (where Nanjing Normal University is located). Shen Xi'en helped bury 400 Hui bodies including children, women and men. Shen recalled burying a 7 or 8 year old boy in addition to his mother among the Hui bodies.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-197)

Japanese used machine guns to massacre Muslim Suluk children and women at a mosque in the aftermath of the [Jesselton revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jesselton_revolt "Jesselton revolt").[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-198)

### Indonesia

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Indonesia")]

Main article: [Walisongo school massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walisongo_school_massacre "Walisongo school massacre")

The [Walisongo school massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walisongo_school_massacre "Walisongo school massacre") was the slaughter carried out by [Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians "Christians") militants on May 28, 2000, upon several predominantly [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim "Muslim") villages around [Poso](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poso "Poso") town, [Central Sulawesi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Sulawesi "Central Sulawesi"), [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia") as part of a [broader sectarian conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poso_riots "Poso riots") in the Poso region. Officially, the total number killed in the attacks is 367.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-voa-199)

### Syria

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Syria")]

Main article: [1982 Hama massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Hama_massacre "1982 Hama massacre")

[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/After_Hama_Massacre_18.jpg/250px-After_Hama_Massacre_18.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:After_Hama_Massacre_18.jpg)

[Anti-Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Islam_sentiment "Anti-Islam sentiment")[Ba'athist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Ba%27athism "Neo-Ba'athism") writings on the walls of [Hama city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hama "Hama") following the [Hama Massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Hama_massacre "1982 Hama massacre") in 1982. The propaganda slogan, which translates to "There is no god but the homeland, and there is no messenger but the Ba'ath party", denigrated the _[Shahada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shahada "Shahada")_ (Islamic testimony of faith).

[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/After_Hama_Massacre_3.jpg/250px-After_Hama_Massacre_3.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:After_Hama_Massacre_3.jpg)

A photo showing the destruction of [Hama city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hama "Hama") after the massacre

The [Hama massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Hama_massacre "1982 Hama massacre")[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto5-200) ([Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): مجزرة حماة) was a [genocidal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide")[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto6-201) campaign of extermination launched by [Ba'athist Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba%27athist_Syria "Ba'athist Syria") in February 1982, under orders of Syrian dictator [Hafez al-Assad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad "Hafez al-Assad") to crush an uprising by the [Muslim Brotherhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood_in_Syria "Muslim Brotherhood in Syria") in [Sunni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni_Islam "Sunni Islam")-majority town of Hama. Hama was [besieged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege "Siege") for 27 days by [Syrian military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_Armed_Forces "Syrian Armed Forces") and [Ba'athist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Syria_Region "Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party – Syria Region") paramilitaries, during which period the city was isolated from the outside.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-fisk2010-202)[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-memri2002-203) The ground operations of the massacre were supervised by [Rifaat al-Assad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rifaat_al-Assad "Rifaat al-Assad"), the brother of [Hafez al-Assad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad "Hafez al-Assad"), who commanded sectarian [Alawite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alawites "Alawites")[deathsquads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_squad "Death squad") such as the [Defense Companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defense_Companies_(Syria) "Defense Companies (Syria)").[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-204)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto5-200)

Prior to the start of operations, [Hafez al-Assad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafez_al-Assad "Hafez al-Assad") issued orders to seal off Hama from the outside world; effectively imposing a [media blackout](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Media_blackout "Media blackout"), total shut down of communications, electricity and food supplies to the city for months. Then the massacre campaign was launched, which involved indiscriminate attacks, military bombardment, aerial attacks, etc.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Moss-205) The indiscriminate bombings and [mass-shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_shooting "Mass shooting") by paramilitaries had razed much of the city to the ground and killed tens of thousands of civilians.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-206)[Patrick Seale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrick_Seale "Patrick Seale"), reporting in _[The Globe and Mail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Globe\_and\_Mail "The Globe and Mail"),_ described the operation as a "two-week orgy of killing, destruction and looting" which destroyed the city and killed a minimum of 25,000 inhabitants.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Moss-205) However, contemporary estimates put the total death toll to at least 40,000 civilians.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-memri2002-203)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-207)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-208) The massacre is the "single deadliest act" of violence perpetrated by any Arab regime upon its own population, in [Modern Arab history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Middle_East "Modern Middle East").[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-wright2008-209)[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-210)

The attack has been described as a "[genocidal massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocidal_massacre "Genocidal massacre")"[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto6-201) which was motivated by [anti-Sunni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Sunnism "Anti-Sunnism") sectarianism of Alawite-dominated elites of the [Arab Socialist Ba'ath party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Socialist_Ba%27ath_Party_%E2%80%93_Syria_Region "Arab Socialist Ba'ath Party – Syria Region").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto-211)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-212)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto4-213)[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto5-200) The militant secularist ideology of [neo-Ba'athism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-ba%27athism "Neo-ba'athism") which advocated the elimination of religion and establishment of [socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism "Socialism") in the society also played a role in the brutality of the massacre.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-214) Memory of the massacre remains an important aspect of Syrian culture and evokes strong emotions amongst Syrians to the present day.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto7-215)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto3-216) Women, children and all Hama inhabitants irrespective of their political leanings were targeted indiscriminately during the military onslaught. Even Ba'ath party members and their families became victims of slaughter and mass-shootings of Rifaat al-Assad's paramilitaries.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto3-216) Internationally, the Hama massacre became a symbol of the [Assad regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assad_regime "Assad regime")'s brutal repression and disregard of civilian lives.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-hrw19962-217)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-218)

### Myanmar

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Myanmar")]

Main articles: [Religion in Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Myanmar "Religion in Myanmar") and [Freedom of religion in Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Myanmar "Freedom of religion in Myanmar")

Further information: [Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims_in_Myanmar "Persecution of Muslims in Myanmar"), [Rohingya conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rohingya_conflict "Rohingya conflict"), and [Rohingya genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rohingya_genocide "Rohingya genocide")

[Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myanmar "Myanmar") has a [Buddhist majority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism_in_Myanmar "Buddhism in Myanmar"). The [Muslim minority in Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Myanmar "Islam in Myanmar") mostly consists of the [Rohingya people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rohingya_people "Rohingya people") and the descendants of Muslim immigrants from [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India") (including the modern-day nations of [Bangladesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh "Bangladesh")) and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") (the ancestors of [Chinese Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_China "Islam in China") in Myanmar came from [Yunnan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yunnan "Yunnan") province), as well as the descendants of earlier [Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs "Arabs") and [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_people "Persian people") settlers. [Indian Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_India "Islam in India") were brought to Burma by the British in order to aid them in clerical work and business. After independence, many Muslims retained their previous positions and achieved prominence in business and politics.

At first, the Buddhist persecution of Muslims arose for religious reasons, and it occurred during the reign of King [Bayinnaung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayinnaung "Bayinnaung"), 1550–1589 AD. He also disallowed the [Eid al-Adha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Adha "Eid al-Adha"), the religious sacrifice of cattle, regarding the killing of animals in the name of religion as a cruel custom. Halal food was also forbidden by King Alaungpaya in the 18th century.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_010.jpg/250px-Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_010.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_010.jpg)

Rohingya Muslims at the [Kutupalong refugee camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kutupalong_refugee_camp "Kutupalong refugee camp") in Bangladesh, October 2017

When General [Ne Win](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ne_Win "Ne Win") swept to power on a wave of nationalism in 1962, the status of Muslims changed for the worse. Muslims were expelled from the army and rapidly marginalized.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-autogenerated4-219) Many Rohingya Muslims fled Burma as refugees and inundated neighbouring Bangladesh including 200,000 who fled Burma in 1978 as a result of the [King Dragon operation in Arakan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_Dragon_operation_in_Arakan "King Dragon operation in Arakan")[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-220) and 250,000 in 1991.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-221)

A widely publicized Burmese conflict was the [2012 Rakhine State riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Rakhine_State_riots "2012 Rakhine State riots"), a series of clashes that primarily involved the ethnic [Rakhine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rakhine_people "Rakhine people") Buddhist people and the Rohingya Muslim people in the northern [Rakhine State](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rakhine_State "Rakhine State") – an estimated 90,000 people were displaced as a result of the riots.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-222)[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-223)

[Myanmar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myanmar "Myanmar")'s pro-democracy leader [Aung San Suu Kyi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aung_San_Suu_Kyi "Aung San Suu Kyi") was accused of failing to protect Myanmar's Rohingya Muslims during the [2016–17 persecution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Rohingya_persecution_in_Myanmar "2016–17 Rohingya persecution in Myanmar").[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-224) State crime experts from [Queen Mary University of London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queen_Mary_University_of_London "Queen Mary University of London") warned that Suu Kyi is "legitimising genocide" in Myanmar.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-225)

Some Buddhist leaders in Myanmar such as [Ashin Wirathu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashin_Wirathu "Ashin Wirathu") promote violence against Muslims.

### Nazi Germany

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Nazi Germany")]

Main articles: [Religion in Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Nazi_Germany "Religion in Nazi Germany") and [Religious views of Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_views_of_Adolf_Hitler "Religious views of Adolf Hitler")

Further information: [Relations between Nazi Germany and the Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relations_between_Nazi_Germany_and_the_Arab_world "Relations between Nazi Germany and the Arab world")

[Nazi ideology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism "Nazism")'s [racial theories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_racial_theories "Nazi racial theories") considered [ethnic groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group "Ethnic group") which were associated with Islam to be "[racially inferior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untermensch "Untermensch")", particularly [Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs "Arabs").[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-226)

During the [invasion of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_France "Battle of France"), thousands of Muslims, both Arabs and [sub-Saharan Africans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa "Sub-Saharan Africa"), who were serving in French colonial units were captured by the Germans. Massacres of these men were widespread, the most notable of these massacres was committed against Moroccans by [Waffen-SS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waffen-SS "Waffen-SS") troops during the fighting which occurred around Cambrai, the Moroccans were killed in mass after they were driven from the outskirts of the city and surrendered.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-227)

During [Operation Barbarossa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa "Operation Barbarossa"), the [Einsatzgruppen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Einsatzgruppen "Einsatzgruppen") engaged in the mass execution of over 140,000 Soviet POWs,[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-228) many of whom were killed because they had "Asiatic features".[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-229)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-230) Civilian Muslim men were often mistaken for Jews and killed due to the fact that they had previously been circumsized.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-231) In 1942 in [Amersfoort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amersfoort "Amersfoort") in the [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands"), 101 Soviet [Uzbek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzbeks "Uzbeks") Muslim soldiers were massacred by Nazi Germans after they were forced into a concentration camp and displayed to the local [Dutch people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_people "Dutch people") as proof the Soviets were made out of "untermenschen".[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-232) Various Muslim ethnic groups were targeted for extermination, such as the [Turkmens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmens "Turkmens").[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-233)

### Philippines

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Philippines")]

Main article: [Religion in the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_the_Philippines "Religion in the Philippines")

Further information: [Moro people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_people "Moro people"), [Spanish–Moro conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93Moro_conflict "Spanish–Moro conflict"), [Moro Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_Rebellion "Moro Rebellion"), [Moros during World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moros_during_World_War_II "Moros during World War II"), [Moro insurgency in the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_insurgency_in_the_Philippines "Moro insurgency in the Philippines"), [Ilaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilaga "Ilaga"), [Jabidah massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabidah_massacre "Jabidah massacre"), [Manili massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manili_massacre "Manili massacre"), and [Malisbong massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malisbong_massacre "Malisbong massacre")

[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Bud_Dajo_Massacre_Trench_on_Jolo_Island_c1906.png/250px-Bud_Dajo_Massacre_Trench_on_Jolo_Island_c1906.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bud_Dajo_Massacre_Trench_on_Jolo_Island_c1906.png)

U.S. soldiers pose with Moro dead after the [Moro Crater massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_Crater_massacre "Moro Crater massacre") in 1906

The [Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines "Philippines") is a [predominantly Christian society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Philippines "Christianity in the Philippines") with a complicated history of relations between Islam and Christianity. Despite historic evidence of [Islamization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_Philippines "Islam in the Philippines") spreading throughout the islands in the 13th–16th centuries, the archipelago [came under Spanish rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898) "History of the Philippines (1521–1898)") in the 16th century. The Spanish proselytized many natives, and labelled those who remained Muslims as _Moro_, a derogatory term recalling the [Moors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moors "Moors"), an Islamic people of [North Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "North Africa") who occupied parts of Spain for several centuries. Today, this term _Moro_ is used to refer to the indigenous Muslim tribes and ethnic groups of the country. When the Spanish came to the Philippine islands, most of the natives in Luzon and Visayas were pagans with Muslim minorities, and while Spanish proselytized many natives, many Muslims in Luzon and Visayas were not exempted by the Spaniards from the [Spanish Inquisition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition "Spanish Inquisition"), wherein Muslims to become Catholics or else die for their faith. Those who remained Muslims are only the natives of [Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mindanao "Mindanao") and [Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulu "Sulu") which the Spaniards failed to subjugate, or had control of only briefly and partially.

The [Spanish–Moro Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93Moro_Wars "Spanish–Moro Wars") between Spanish colonial authorities and the indigenous Sultanates of the [Moro peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_people "Moro people") (the [Sultanate of Sulu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Sulu "Sultanate of Sulu"), confederation of sultanates in Lanao and [Sultanate of Maguindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultanate_of_Maguindanao "Sultanate of Maguindanao")) further escalated tensions between the Christian and Muslim groups of the country. The Moros fought in the [Moro Rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_Rebellion "Moro Rebellion") against the Americans during which Americans massacred Moro women and children at the [Moro Crater massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_Crater_massacre "Moro Crater massacre"), [against the Japanese in World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moros_during_World_War_II "Moros during World War II"), and are [waging an insurgency against the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_insurgency_in_the_Philippines "Moro insurgency in the Philippines").

The pro-Philippine government [Ilaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilaga "Ilaga") militia, composed of Catholic and other Christian settlers on Moro land in Mindanao, were known for their atrocities and massacres against Moro civilians. The Ilaga's bloodiest attack happened in June 1971 when they slaughtered 65 Moro civilians in a Mosque during the [Manili massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manili_massacre "Manili massacre"). On 24 September 1974, in the [Malisbong massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malisbong_massacre "Malisbong massacre"), the [Armed Forces of the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Philippines "Armed Forces of the Philippines") slaughtered about 1,500 Moro Muslim civilians who were praying in a Mosque, in addition to [mass raping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wartime_sexual_violence#Philippines:_Mindanao_and_Sulu "Wartime sexual violence") Moro girls who had been taken aboard a boat.[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-234)

Polls have shown that some non-Muslim Filipinos hold negative views directed against the Moro people.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-235)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-kas.de-236)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-237)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-238)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-239)[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-240)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

### Russia

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Russia")]

#### Russian Empire

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Russian Empire")]

[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Firinat_xalikov_war.jpg/250px-Firinat_xalikov_war.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Firinat_xalikov_war.jpg)

[Qol Şärif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kul_Sharif "Kul Sharif") and his students defend their mosque during the [Siege of Kazan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Kazan "Siege of Kazan").

Further information: [Circassian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassian_genocide "Circassian genocide"), [Chechen genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chechen_genocide "Chechen genocide"), and [Caucasian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasian_War "Caucasian War")

The period from the [conquest of Kazan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Kazan_Wars "Russo-Kazan Wars") in 1552 to the ascension of [Catherine the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catherine_the_Great "Catherine the Great") in 1762, was marked by systematic repression of Muslims through policies of exclusion and discrimination as well as the destruction of Muslim culture by elimination of outward manifestations of Islam such as mosques. The first wave of persecution and forced conversions of Muslims to Christianity occurred soon after the Russian conquest of the [Kazan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khanate_of_Kazan "Khanate of Kazan") and [Astrakhan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrakhan_Khanate "Astrakhan Khanate") Khanates.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:03-241)

Another period of intense mosque destruction and anti-Muslim oppression from the Russian authorities occurred during the 18th century. During the reign of [Anna of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anna_of_Russia "Anna of Russia"), many Muslims were forced or pressured to convert.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:13-242) New converts were exempted from paying taxes, were granted certain privileges, and were given better resources for the learning of their new faith. Many continued to secretly practice Islam and were [crypto-Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crypto-Islam "Crypto-Islam").[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:13-242)

The Russians initially demonstrated a willingness in allowing Islam to flourish as Muslim clerics were invited into the various region to preach to the Muslims, particularly the [Kazakhs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakhs "Kazakhs") whom the Russians viewed as "savages" and "ignorant" of morals and ethics.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-243)[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-EncycSex572-244) However, Russian policy shifted toward weakening Islam by introducing pre-Islamic elements of collective consciousness.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Hunter14-245) Such attempts included methods of eulogizing pre-Islamic historical figures and imposing a sense of inferiority by sending Kazakhs to highly elite Russian military institutions.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Hunter14-245) In response, Kazakh religious leaders attempted to bring religious fervor by espousing [pan-Turkism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Turkism "Pan-Turkism"), though many were persecuted as a result.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-246)

While total expulsion as in other Christian nations such as Spain, Portugal, and Sicily was not feasible to achieve a homogeneous [Russian Orthodox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church "Russian Orthodox Church") population, other policies such as land grants and the promotion of migration by other Russian and non-Muslim populations into Muslim lands displaced many Muslims making them minorities in places such as some parts of the South Ural region to other parts such as the [Ottoman Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), and almost annihilating the [Circassians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassians "Circassians"), [Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatars "Crimean Tatars"), and various Muslims of the Caucasus. The Russian army rounded up people, driving Muslims from their villages to ports on the Black Sea, where they awaited ships provided by the neighbouring [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"). The explicit Russian goal was to expel the groups in question from their lands.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-247) They were given a choice as to where to be resettled: in the Ottoman Empire or in Russia far from their old lands. Only a small percentage (the numbers are unknown) accepted resettlement within the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire"). The trend of [Russification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russification "Russification") has continued at different paces during the remaining Tsarist period and under the Soviet Union, so that today there are more Tatars living outside the [Republic of Tatarstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatarstan "Tatarstan") than inside it.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-248)

Alexander Suvorov announced the capture of Ismail in 1791 to the Tsarina Catherine in a doggerel couplet, after the assault had been pressed from house to house, room to room, and nearly every Muslim man, woman, and child in the city had been killed in three days of uncontrolled massacre, 40,000 [Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") dead, a few hundred taken into captivity. For all his bluffness, Suvorov later told an English traveller that when the massacre was over he went back to his tent and wept.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-J._Goodwin,_p._244-249)

During the [Circassian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Circassian_genocide "Circassian genocide"), general [Grigory Zass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grigory_Zass "Grigory Zass") in sent the severed Circassian heads to Berlin for anatomical studies.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-250) The [Decembrist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decembrist "Decembrist")[Nikolai Ivanovich Lorer](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nikolai_Ivanovich_Lorer&action=edit&redlink=1 "Nikolai Ivanovich Lorer (page does not exist)")[[ru](https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%9B%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B5%D1%80,_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B9_%D0%98%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87 "ru:Лорер, Николай Иванович")] said that Zass cleaned and boiled the flesh off the heads after storing them under his bed in his tent. He also had Circassian heads outside of his tent impaled on lances on a hill. Circassian men's corpses were decapitated by Russian-Cossack women on the battlefield after the battles were over for the heads to be sent to Zass for collection.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-251)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-252)[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-253)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-254)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Zass erected Circassian heads on poles outside of his tent and witnesses saw the wind blowing the beards of the heads.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-255) Russian soldiers and Cossacks were paid for sending Circassian heads to General Zass.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-256)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-257)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-258)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-259)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Besides cutting Circassian heads off and collecting them, Zass employed a deliberate strategy of annihilating Circassian en masse, burning entire Circassian villages with the people in it and encouraging violation of Circassian women and children.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-260)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-261) Zass' forces referred to all Circassian elderly, children women, and men as "Bandits, "plunderers", or "thieves" and the Russian empire's forces were commanded by ferociously partholofical officers who commanded political dissidents and criminals.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-262)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-263)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-264)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-265)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-266)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-267)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-268)[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-269)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-270)[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-271)[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-272)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-273)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-274)[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-275)[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-276)[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-277)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Cossacks raped Circassian women and impregnated them with children.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Routledge-278) Circassian children were scared of Zass and he was called the devil (Iblis) by the Circassians.

Russians raped Circassian girls during the [1877 Russo-Turkish war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878) "Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)") from the Circassian refugees who were settled in the Ottoman Balkans.[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-279) Circassian girls were sold into Turkish harems by their relatives.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-280)[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-281) Circassians also raped and murdered Bulgarians during the 1877 Russo-Turkish war.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-282)[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-283)[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-284)[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-285)[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-286)[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-287)[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-288)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Circassian women in the Balkans were raped by Russian soldiers in the Russo-Turkish war of 1877.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-289)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-290)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-291)[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-292)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

#### Soviet Union

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Soviet Union")]

Further information: [Deportation of the Crimean Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Crimean_Tatars "Deportation of the Crimean Tatars") and [Operation Lentil (Caucasus)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deportation_of_the_Chechens_and_Ingush "Deportation of the Chechens and Ingush")

See also: [Islam in the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_Soviet_Union "Islam in the Soviet Union") and [Population transfer in the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union "Population transfer in the Soviet Union")

The Soviet Union was hostile to all forms of religion, which was "[the opium of the masses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opium_of_the_people "Opium of the people")" in accordance with [Marxist ideology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxism "Marxism"). Relative religious freedom existed for Muslims in the years following the revolution, but in the late 1920s the Soviet government took a strong anti-religious turn. Many mosques were closed or torn down.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-293) During the period of [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin")'s leadership, [Crimean Tatar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimean_Tatars "Crimean Tatars"), [Chechen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chechen_people "Chechen people"), [Ingush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ingush_people "Ingush people"), [Balkar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkars "Balkars"), [Karachay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karachays "Karachays"), and [Meskhetian Turk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meskhetian_Turks "Meskhetian Turks") Muslims were victims of mass deportation. Though it principally targeted ethno-religious minorities, the deportations were officially based on alleged [collaborationism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collaboration_with_Nazi_Germany_and_Fascist_Italy "Collaboration with Nazi Germany and Fascist Italy")[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE-294) during the [Nazi occupation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German-occupied_Europe "German-occupied Europe") of Crimea.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-295) The deportation began on 17 May 1944 in all [Crimean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crimea "Crimea") inhabited localities. More than 32,000 [NKVD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NKVD "NKVD") troops participated in this action. 193,865 Crimean Tatars were deported, 151,136 of them to [Uzbek SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic"), 8,597 to [Mari ASSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mari_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Mari Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic"), 4,286 to [Kazakh SSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kazakh_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic"), the rest 29,846 to the various [oblasts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oblast "Oblast") of the [Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic").

From May to November, 10,105 Crimean Tatars died of starvation in Uzbekistan (7% of deported to Uzbek SSR). Nearly 30,000 (20%) died in exile during the year and a half by the NKVD data and nearly 46% by the data of the Crimean Tatar activists. According to Soviet dissident information, many Crimean Tatars were made to work in the large-scale projects conducted by the Soviet [Gulag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulag "Gulag") system of slave labour camps.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-296)

### South-eastern Europe (Balkans)

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: South-eastern Europe (Balkans)")]

See also: [Persecution of Ottoman Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Ottoman_Muslims "Persecution of Ottoman Muslims"), [Massacres during the Greek Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massacres_during_the_Greek_Revolution "Massacres during the Greek Revolution"), [Navarino massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navarino_massacre "Navarino massacre"), [Siege of Tripolitsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Tripolitsa "Siege of Tripolitsa"), [Expulsion of the Albanians 1877–1878](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Albanians_1877%E2%80%931878 "Expulsion of the Albanians 1877–1878"), [Massacres of Albanians in the Balkan Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massacres_of_Albanians_in_the_Balkan_Wars "Massacres of Albanians in the Balkan Wars"), [Chetnik war crimes in World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chetnik_war_crimes_in_World_War_II "Chetnik war crimes in World War II"), [Massacres of Albanians in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massacres_of_Albanians_in_World_War_I "Massacres of Albanians in World War I"), and [Persecution of Albanians in the Kingdom of Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Albanians_in_the_Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia "Persecution of Albanians in the Kingdom of Yugoslavia")

[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg/250px-Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Srebrenica_Massacre_-_Reinterment_and_Memorial_Ceremony_-_July_2007_-_Male_Mourners.jpg)

Mourners at the reburial ceremony for an exhumed victim of the [Srebrenica massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre "Srebrenica massacre") in [Bosnia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Bosnia and Herzegovina")

As the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") entered a permanent phase of decline in the late 17th century it was engaged in a protracted state of conflict, losing territories both in [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe "Europe") and the [Caucasus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caucasus "Caucasus"). The victors were the Christian states, the old [Habsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habsburg "Habsburg") and [Romanov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanov "Romanov") Empires, and the new nation-states of Greece, Serbia, Romania, and Bulgaria.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-297) Rival European powers encouraged the development of nationalist ideologies among the Ottoman subjects in which the Muslims were portrayed as an ethnic "fifth column" left over from a previous era that could not be integrated into the planned future states. The struggle to rid themselves of Ottomans became an important element of the self-identification of the Christians of the [Balkans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkans "Balkans").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-298)

According to Mark Levene, the Victorian public in the 1870s paid much more attention to the massacres and expulsions of Christians than to massacres and expulsions of Muslims, even if on a greater scale. He further suggests that such massacres were even favoured by some circles. Mark Levene also argues that the dominant powers, by supporting "nation-statism" at the [Congress of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin "Congress of Berlin"), legitimized "the primary instrument of Balkan nation-building": [ethnic cleansing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing").[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-299) Hall points out that atrocities were committed by all sides during the Balkan conflicts. Deliberate terror was designed to instigate population movements out of particular territories. The aim of targeting the civilian population was to carve ethnically homogeneous countries.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-300)

[Muslims were forced to leave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exodus_of_Muslims_from_Serbia_(1862) "Exodus of Muslims from Serbia (1862)") Principality of Serbia in 1862.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-301) Muslim Albanians, along smaller numbers of urban Turks (some with Albanian heritage), [were expelled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Albanians,_1877%E2%80%931878 "Expulsion of the Albanians, 1877–1878") by the [Serb army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armed_forces_of_the_Principality_of_Serbia "Armed forces of the Principality of Serbia") from most parts of the [Sanjak of Niş](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanjak_of_Ni%C5%A1 "Sanjak of Niš") and fled to the [Kosovo Vilayet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet "Kosovo Vilayet") and Macedonia during and after the [Serbian–Ottoman War (1876–78)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbian%E2%80%93Ottoman_War_(1876%E2%80%9378) "Serbian–Ottoman War (1876–78)").[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Jagodic1998-302) An estimated 49–130,000[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-303)[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-304)[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-305)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Batakovic1992-306)[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Elsie2010-307)[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-308)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Albanians were either expelled, fled and/or retreated from the captured areas seeking refuge in [Ottoman Kosovo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kosovo_Vilayet "Kosovo Vilayet").[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Jagodic1998-302)[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Muller-309) The departure of the Albanian population from these regions was done in a manner that today would be characterized as ethnic cleansing.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Muller-309)

Justin McCarty estimates that between 1821 and 1922 around five and a half million Muslims were driven out of Europe and five million more were killed or died of disease and starvation while fleeing.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-310) Cleansing occurred as a result of the Serbian and Greek independence in the 1820s and 1830s, the [Russo-Turkish War 1877–1878](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878) "Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)"), and culminating in the [Balkan Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Balkan Wars") 1912–1913. Mann describes these acts as "murderous ethnic cleansing on stupendous scale not previously seen in Europe" referring to the 1914 [Carnegie Endowment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment "Carnegie Endowment") report.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-311)[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-312) It is estimated that at the turn of the 20th century there were 4,4 million Muslims living in the Balkan regions under Ottoman control.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Cornis-Pope,_Marcel_Neubauer_pp.21-313) More than one million Muslims left the Balkans in the last three decades of the 19th century.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-314) Between 1912 and 1926 nearly 2.9 million Muslims were either killed or forced to emigrate to Turkey.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Cornis-Pope,_Marcel_Neubauer_pp.21-313)

Between 10,000[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-315) and 30,000[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-316)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-317)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-318) Turks were killed in [Tripolitsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tripolitsa "Tripolitsa") by Greek rebels in the summer of 1821, including the entire Jewish population of the city. Similar events as these occurred elsewhere during the Greek Revolution resulting in the eradication and expulsion of virtually the entire Turkish population of the [Morea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morea "Morea"). These acts ensured the ethnic homogenization of the area under the rule of the future modern Greek state.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-319) According to claims by Turkish delegations, in 1878 the Muslim inhabitants in [Thessaly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thessaly "Thessaly") are estimated to be 150,000 and in 1897 the Muslims numbered 50,000 in Crete. By 1919 there were virtually no Muslims left in Thessaly and only 20,000 in Crete.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-320)

In the [Bulgarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarians "Bulgarians") insurgency of the [April Uprising](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/April_Uprising "April Uprising") in 1876 an estimate of 1,000 Muslims were killed.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-321)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-322) During the [Russo-Turkish War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%931878) "Russo-Turkish War (1877–1878)") large numbers of Turks were either killed, perished, or became refugees. There are different estimates about the casualties of the war. Crampton describes an exodus of 130,000–150,000 expelled of which approximately half returned for an intermediary period encouraged by the [Congress of Berlin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin "Congress of Berlin"). Hupchick and McCarthy point out that 260,000 perished and 500,000 became refugees.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-323)[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-324) The Turkish scholars Karpat and Ipek argue that up to 300,000 were killed and 1–1.5 million were forced to emigrate.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-325)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-326) Members of the European press who covered the war in Bulgaria reported on the Russian atrocities against Muslims. Witness accounts from Schumla and Razgrad describe children, women, and elderly wounded by sabres and lances. They stated that the entire Muslim population of many villages had been massacred.[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-327) Recently uncovered photographs in the archive of the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs from the Russo-Turkish War 1877–1878 show the massacre of Muslims by the Russians in the region of [Stara Zagora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stara_Zagora "Stara Zagora") claiming to have affected some 20,000 Muslim civilians.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-328)

Massacres against Turks and Muslims during the [Balkan Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Balkan Wars") in the hands of Bulgarians, Greeks, and Armenians are described in detail in the 1912 Carnegie Endowment report.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-329) The Bulgarian violence during the [Balkan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balkan_War "Balkan War") included burning of villages, transforming mosques into churches, rape of women, and mutilation of bodies. It is estimated that 220,000 [Pomaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pomaks "Pomaks") were forcefully [Christianized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianized "Christianized") and forbidden to wear Islamic religious clothing.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-330)

During [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), the [Chetniks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chetniks "Chetniks"), a Yugoslav Royalist and Serbian nationalist movement, committed numerous [war crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chetnik_war_crimes_in_World_War_II "Chetnik war crimes in World War II") primarily directed against the non-Serb population of the Kingdom of Yugoslavia explicitly ordering the ethnic cleansing, mainly 29,000–33,000 Muslims were killed.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-331)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-332)

Also during World War II, Muslims faced sporadic but significant and violent persecution at the hands of the Croatian fascist [Ustaše](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Usta%C5%A1e "Ustaše") movement in the [Independent State of Croatia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia "Independent State of Croatia"). Despite Ustaše overtures and positive propaganda towards Muslims, the government in Zagreb in reality staunchly favored Catholics in the military, government and ministry positions, with Muslim militias being regarded as little more than cannon fodder with little to no combat effectiveness. Catholics held the vast majority of high ranking government offices, leading to complaints and protests from Muslim religious leaders. The archbishop of Sarajevo had stated that the situation had become critical for Muslims due to violent persecution from both the Serbian Chetniks and Croatian fascists. According to some reports, as many as 100,000 Muslims had been killed and 250,000 displaced by the Ustaše by 1943. There were also reports of forced conversions of Muslims to Catholicism. One German officer reportedly remarked that “the Muslims bear the special status of being persecuted by all others.”[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-333)

### Tatarstan

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Tatarstan")]

Main article: [1921–1922 famine in Tatarstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1921%E2%80%931922_famine_in_Tatarstan "1921–1922 famine in Tatarstan")

The 1921–1922 famine in Tatarstan was a period of mass starvation and drought that took place in the [Tatar ASSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatar_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Tatar Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic") as a result of [war communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_communism "War communism") policy,[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMizelle200218-334)[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-335) in which 500,000[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-336) to 2,000,000[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMizelle2002281-337) peasants died. The event was part of the greater [Russian famine of 1921–1922](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921%E2%80%931922 "Russian famine of 1921–1922") that affected other parts of the USSR,[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillar200456-338) in which up 5,000,000 people died in total.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMillar2004270-339)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-340) According to [Roman Serbyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Serbyn "Roman Serbyn"), a professor of Russian and East European history, the Tatarstan famine was the first man-made famine in the Soviet Union and systematically targeted ethnic minorities such as [Volga Tatars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga_Tatars "Volga Tatars") and [Volga Germans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volga_Germans "Volga Germans").[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-341) The 1921–1922 famine in [Tatarstan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tatarstan "Tatarstan") has been compared to [Holodomor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holodomor "Holodomor") in [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine "Ukraine"),[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-342) and in 2008, the [All-Russian Tatar Social Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=All-Russian_Tatar_Social_Center&action=edit&redlink=1 "All-Russian Tatar Social Center (page does not exist)") (VTOTs) asked the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") to condemn the 1921–22 Tatarstan famine as genocide of Muslim Tatars.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-343)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-344)

### Turkey

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Turkey")]

During [World War One](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), both [Turks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") and [Kurds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurds "Kurds") were killed by [Russians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russians "Russians"), [Assyrians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assyrians "Assyrians") and [Armenians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenians "Armenians") in the eastern provinces of the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire"), however, this was mainly in retaliation for Turkish persecution of Christians ([Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide") and [Greek genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_genocide "Greek genocide")).[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-345)[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-346)

On 14 May 1919, the Greek army landed in [İzmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C4%B0zmir "İzmir") ([Smyrna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smyrna "Smyrna")), which marked the beginning of the [Greco-Turkish War (1919–1922)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Turkish_War_(1919%E2%80%931922) "Greco-Turkish War (1919–1922)"). During the war, the Greek side committed a number of atrocities in western provinces (such as İzmir, Manisa, and Uşak),[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Vice-Consul_James_Loder_Park_1923-347) the local Muslim population was subjected to massacre, ravaging and rape.[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-348)

See also: [Persecution of Ottoman Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Ottoman_Muslims "Persecution of Ottoman Muslims"), [Menemen massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menemen_massacre "Menemen massacre"), [Yalova Peninsula massacres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yalova_Peninsula_massacres "Yalova Peninsula massacres"), [Fire of Manisa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fire_of_Manisa "Fire of Manisa"), and [Greco-Turkish War (1919–22)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Turkish_War_(1919%E2%80%9322) "Greco-Turkish War (1919–22)")

The Republic of Turkey was founded on a strict interpretation of secularism by the war-hero turned statesman, [Mustafa Kemal Atatürk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk "Mustafa Kemal Atatürk"). In the early republican era, the revolutionary Kemalist government had sought to actively de-Islamize society and turn Turkey into a fully Westernized country. The Kemalists had perceived religion, Islam in particular, to be a force of backwardness. As such, they cracked down on many outward expressions of Islam, whether orthodox or heterodox-folk manifestations of it. They wanted religion to be solely limited to the "conscience of individuals".[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:5-349) The fifth Turkish prime minister, [Şükrü Saracoğlu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%9E%C3%BCkr%C3%BC_Saraco%C4%9Flu "Şükrü Saracoğlu"), had allegedly desired the abolition of religion altogether through government restrictions.[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-350) The government had all shariah courts (including those relating to personal civil law) and traditional madrasas dissolved. The teaching of Arabic, and the Arabic adhaan, was also banned.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:5-349) The fez (an Ottoman Islamic head gear) was also banned, with European hats being mandated instead. Those who opposed this mandate were dealt with harshly.[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-351) However, the military regime under [Kenan Evren](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kenan_Evren "Kenan Evren") had softened its stance on Islam, seeing it as an alternative to communism.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-352) The Turkish generals had also promoted Turkish-Sunni Islam to counter Islamism, amidst the Iranian Revolution.[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-353)

### Vietnam

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Vietnam")]

Main articles: [Cham–Vietnamese War (1471)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cham%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War_(1471) "Cham–Vietnamese War (1471)") and [History of the Cham–Vietnamese wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Cham%E2%80%93Vietnamese_wars "History of the Cham–Vietnamese wars")

The Vietnamese Emperor [Minh Mạng](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minh_M%E1%BA%A1ng "Minh Mạng") unleashed persecution of Cham Muslims after he conquered the final remnants of [Champa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Champa "Champa") in 1832.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-354)[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-355) The Vietnamese coercively fed lizard and pig meat to Cham Muslims and cow meat to Cham Hindus against their will to punish them and assimilate them to Vietnamese culture.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Wook2004-356)

Current situation
-----------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Current situation")]

### Africa

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Africa")]

#### Burkina Faso

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Burkina Faso")]

On 11 October 2019 [a mass shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burkina_Faso_mosque_attack "Burkina Faso mosque attack") occurred in a [mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosque "Mosque") in northern [Burkina Faso](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burkina_Faso "Burkina Faso") which left 16 people dead and two injured.[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-BBC-357) It happened while the residents were praying inside the Grand Mosque in Salmossi, a village close to the border with [Mali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mali "Mali"). _[AFP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agence\_France-Presse "Agence France-Presse")_ reported that 13 people died on the spot while 3 died later due to the injuries.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-France_24-358)

#### Central African Republic

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Central African Republic")]

During the internal armed [conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present) "Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)") in the [Central African Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_African_Republic "Central African Republic") in 2013, [anti-balaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-balaka "Anti-balaka") militiamen were targeting Bangui's [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_the_Central_African_Republic "Islam in the Central African Republic") neighbourhoods[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-359) and Muslim ethnic groups such as the [Fulas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fula_people "Fula people").[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-360)

Early 2014 marked a turning point; hardened by war and massacres, the anti-balaka committed multiple atrocities.[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-time140529-361) In 2014, Amnesty International reported several massacres committed by anti-balaka against Muslim civilians, forcing thousands of Muslims to flee the country.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-362)

On 24 June 2014, anti-balaka gunmen killed 17 Muslim [Fula people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fula_people "Fula people") at a camp in [Bambari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bambari "Bambari"). Some of the bodies were mutilated and burnt by the assailants.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-363)

On 11 October 2017, 25 Muslim civilians were massacred by anti-balaka militiamen inside a mosque in the town of [Kembe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kemb%C3%A9 "Kembé").[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-364)

#### Chad

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Chad")]

In February 1979, anti-Muslim riots occurred in southern Chad, as a result hundreds or thousands of Muslim civilians died.[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-365)

#### Ethiopia

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Ethiopia")]

In April 2022, a group of Christian extremists opened fire at a Muslim funeral, killing more than 20 people. Amidst sectarian tensions, two mosques were burnt down and another two were damaged.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:7-366) “'In the apparent retaliatory attacks that followed, two Orthodox Christian men were reportedly burnt to death, another man hacked to death, and five churches burnt down'” in the southwest of the country.[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:7-366) It is clear that tensions between Muslims and Christians in Ethiopia is high and evil is being done by people identifying with both religions.

#### Mali

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Mali")]

On 23 March 2019, [several attacks by gunmen killed at least 160 and injured at least 55](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ogossagou_massacre "Ogossagou massacre") Muslim [Fulani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fula_people "Fula people") herdsmen, because of the allegations that the villagers were involved in supporting [Islamic terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_terrorism "Islamic terrorism"). Two villages, Ogossagou and Welingara, were particularly affected.[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-AP-Baba_Ahmed2-367)[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-368)[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-369)

### Asia

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Asia")]

[![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_09%29.jpg/250px-Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_09%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rohingya_displaced_Muslims_09).jpg)

[Rohingya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rohingya_people "Rohingya people") refugees in Bangladesh, October 2017

[![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Cast_Lead_Mosque.jpg/250px-Cast_Lead_Mosque.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cast_Lead_Mosque.jpg)

Mosque in [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_Strip "Gaza Strip"), destroyed during the [Gaza War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_War_(2008%E2%80%9309) "Gaza War (2008–09)"), 2009

#### Azerbaijan

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Azerbaijan")]

Main article: [Islam in Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Azerbaijan "Islam in Azerbaijan")

In [Nardaran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nardaran "Nardaran"), a deadly incident broke out in 2015 between Azerbaijan security forces and religious Shia residents in which two policemen and four suspected Shia Muslim militants were killed.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-370)[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-371)[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-372)[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-373)[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-374)[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-375)[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-376)[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-377)[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-378)[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-379)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

As a result of this incident, the Azerbaijani parliament passed laws prohibiting people with religious education received abroad to implement Islamic rites and ceremonies in Azerbaijan, as well as to preach in mosques and occupy leading positions in the country; as well as prohibiting the display of religious paraphernalia, flags, and slogans, except in places of worship, religious centers, and offices.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-380)[Ashura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Day_of_Ashura "Day of Ashura") festivities in public have also been banned.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-381) The Azerbaijani government also passed a law to remove the citizenship of Azerbaijani citizens who fight abroad.[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-382)

The Azerbaijan authorities cracked down on observant Sunni Muslims.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-383)

#### China

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: China")]

##### Hainan Island

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Hainan Island")]

[Hainan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hainan "Hainan") is China's southernmost region inhabited by the [Utsul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utsul "Utsul") Muslim population of approximately 10,000. In September 2020, the [hijab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab "Hijab") was banned from schools in the region.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-SCMP-384)

Earlier in 2019, a CCP document titled "Working Document regarding the strengthening of overall governance over Huixin and Huihui Neighbourhood" described a number of measures to be taken on the Utsuls, including increased surveillance of residents in Muslim neighbourhoods, ban on traditional dress in schools and government offices, rebuilding of mosques to a smaller size and without "Arabic tendencies", removal of Arabic script from shopfronts, along with words like "[halal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Halal "Halal")" and "Islamic".[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-SCMP-384)

##### Tibet

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Tibet")]

When Hui started migrating into [Lhasa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lhasa "Lhasa") in the 1990s, rumours circulated among Tibetans in Lhasa about the Hui, such as that they were [cannibals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_cannibalism "Human cannibalism") or ate children.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Fischer-385): 2, 5, 10, 17–20  In February 2003, Tibetans rioted against Hui, destroying Hui-owned shops and restaurants.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-386) Local [Tibetan Buddhist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhist "Tibetan Buddhist") religious leaders led a regional boycott movement that encouraged Tibetans to boycott Hui-owned shops, spreading the myth that Hui put the ashes of cremated [imams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imam "Imam") in the cooking water they used to serve Tibetans food, in order to convert Tibetans to Islam.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Fischer-385)

In Tibet, the majority of Muslims are [Hui people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hui_people "Hui people"). Hatred between Tibetans and Muslims stems from events during the Muslim warlord [Ma Bufang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma_Bufang "Ma Bufang")'s oppressive rule in Qinghai such as [Ngolok rebellions (1917–49)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ngolok_rebellions_(1917%E2%80%9349) "Ngolok rebellions (1917–49)") and the [Sino-Tibetan War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Tibetan_War "Sino-Tibetan War"), but in 1949 the Communists put an end to the violence between Tibetans and Muslims, however, new Tibetan-Muslim violence broke out after China engaged in liberalization. Riots broke out between Muslims and Tibetans over incidents such as bones in soups and prices of balloons, and Tibetans accused Muslims of being cannibals who cooked humans in their soup and of contaminating food with urine. Tibetans attacked Muslim restaurants. Fires set by Tibetans which burned the apartments and shops of Muslims resulted in Muslim families being killed and wounded in the 2008 mid-March riots. Due to Tibetan violence against Muslims, the traditional Islamic white caps have not been worn by many Muslims. Scarfs were removed and replaced with hairnets by Muslim women in order to hide. Muslims prayed in secret at home when in August 2008 the Tibetans burned the Mosque. Incidents such as these which make Tibetans look bad on the international stage are covered up by the [Tibetan exile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibetan_exile "Tibetan exile") community. The repression of Tibetan separatism by the Chinese government is supported by Hui Muslims.[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Demick-387) In addition, Chinese-speaking Hui have problems with Tibetan Hui (the Tibetan speaking [Kache](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kache "Kache") minority of Muslims).[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Mayaram_2009_75-388)

On 8 October 2012, a mob of about 200 [Tibetan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibetan_people "Tibetan people") monks beat a dozen Dungans (Hui Muslims) in [Luqu County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luqu_County "Luqu County"), [Gansu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gansu "Gansu") province, in retaliation for the Chinese Muslim community's application to build a mosque in the county.[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Ethnic_Clashes_Over_Gansu_Mosque-389)

The main Mosque in Lhasa was burned down by Tibetans and Chinese Hui Muslims were violently assaulted by Tibetan rioters in the [2008 Tibetan unrest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Tibetan_unrest "2008 Tibetan unrest").[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-390) Tibetan exiles and foreign scholars like ignore and do not talk about sectarian violence between Tibetan Buddhists and Muslims.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Fischer-385) The majority of Tibetans viewed the wars against Iraq and Afghanistan after 9/11 positively and it had the effect of galvanizing anti-Muslim attitudes among Tibetans and resulted in an anti-Muslim boycott against Muslim owned businesses.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Fischer-385): 17  Tibetan Buddhists propagate a false libel that Muslims cremate their Imams and use the ashes to convert Tibetans to Islam by making Tibetans inhale the ashes, even though the Tibetans seem to be aware that Muslims practice burial and not cremation since they frequently clash against proposed Muslim cemeteries in their area.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Fischer-385): 19
