Since the Chinese government supports and backs up the Hui Muslims, the Tibetans deliberately attack the Hui Muslims as a way to demonstrate anti-government sentiment and because they have a background of sectarian violence against each other since Ma Bufang's rule due to their separate religions and ethnicity and Tibetans resent Hui economic domination.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-391)

##### Xinjiang

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Xinjiang")]

Main article: [Xinjiang internment camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang_internment_camps "Xinjiang internment camps")

Further information: [Persecution of Uyghurs in China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Uyghurs_in_China "Persecution of Uyghurs in China")

The city of [Karamay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karamay "Karamay") has banned Islamic beards, headwear, and clothing on buses.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-392) China's far-western Xinjiang province have passed a law to prohibit residents from wearing burqas in public.[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-393) China has also banned Ramadan fasting for [Chinese Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_Communist_Party "Chinese Communist Party") (CCP) members in certain parts of Xinjiang.[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-394)[Amnesty International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amnesty_International "Amnesty International") has said [Uyghurs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghurs "Uyghurs") face widespread discrimination in employment, housing, and educational opportunities, as well as curtailed religious freedom and political marginalization.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] Uyghurs who choose to practice their faith can only use a state-approved version of the Koran;[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-395) men who work in the state sector cannot wear beards and women cannot wear headscarves.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-396) The Chinese state controls the management of all mosques, which many Uyghurs feel stifles religious traditions that have formed a crucial part of their identity for centuries. Children under the age of 18 are not allowed to attend religious services at mosques.[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-397) According to [Radio Free Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Free_Asia "Radio Free Asia") in April 2017, the CCP banned Islamic names such as "Saddam", "Hajj", and "Medina" for babies born in Xinjiang.[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-398) Since 2017, it is alleged that China has destroyed or damaged 16,000 [mosques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mosques_in_China "List of mosques in China") in China's Xinjiang province – 65% of the region's total.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-399)[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-400)

According to human rights organizations and western media [Uyghurs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghurs "Uyghurs") face discrimination and religious persecution at the hands of the [government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China "Government of the People's Republic of China") authorities. In a 2013 news article, _The New York Times_ reported, "Many Uighurs are also convinced that Beijing is seeking to wipe out their language and culture through assimilation and education policies that favor Mandarin over Uighur in schools and government jobs. Civil servants can be fired for joining Friday afternoon prayer services, and Uighur college students say they are often required to eat lunch in school cafeterias during the holy month of Ramadan, when observant Muslims fast."[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-401) Chinese authorities have confiscated passports from all residents in largely [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_China "Islam in China") region of [Xinjiang](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xinjiang "Xinjiang"), populated by Turkic-speaking Uyghurs.[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-402)

In August 2018, the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") said that credible reports had led it to estimate that up to a million Uighurs and other Muslims were being held in "something that resembles a massive internment camp that is shrouded in secrecy". The U.N.'s [International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Racial_Discrimination "International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial Discrimination") said that some estimates indicated that up to 2 million Uighurs and other Muslims were held in "political camps for indoctrination", in a "no-rights zone".[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-403) Conditions in Xinjiang had deteriorated that they were described by political scientists as "[Orwellian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orwellian "Orwellian")".[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-HKFP-AFP-404)

These so-called ["re-education" camps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Re-education_through_labor "Re-education through labor") and later, "vocational training centres", were described by the government for "rehabilitation and redemption" to combat terrorism and religious extremism.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-405)[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-406) In response to the UN panel's finding of indefinite detention without due process, the Chinese government delegation officially conceded that it was engaging in widespread "resettlement and re-education" and State media described the controls in Xinjiang as "intense".[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-407)

On 31 August 2018, the United Nations committee called on the Chinese government to "end the practice of detention without lawful charge, trial, and conviction", to release the detained persons, to provide specifics as to the number of interred individuals and the reasons for their detention, and to investigate the allegations of "racial, ethnic, and ethno-religious profiling". A [BBC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC "BBC") report quoted an unnamed Chinese official as saying that "Uighurs enjoyed full rights" but also admitting that "those deceived by religious extremism... shall be assisted by resettlement and re-education".[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-408) On 10 September 2018, UN High Commissioner for Human Rights [Michelle Bachelet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michelle_Bachelet "Michelle Bachelet") urged China to allow observers into Xinjiang and expressed concern about the situation there. She said that: "The UN rights group had shown that Uyghurs and other Muslims are being detained in camps across Xinjiang and I expect discussions with Chinese officials to begin soon".[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-voice-409)[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-410)

The U.S. [Uyghur Human Rights Policy Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uyghur_Human_Rights_Policy_Act "Uyghur Human Rights Policy Act") of 2020 imposes sanctions on foreign individuals and entities responsible for human rights violations in China's Xinjiang region.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-411)

#### Israel

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Israel")]

Discrimination and persecution of Muslims in Israel is rampant. Muslims are not allowed to serve in the IDF and police. In the aftermath of the Hamas-led attack on southern Israel on 7 October 2023, an uptick in Islamophobic comments and sentiment has been observed, in both Israel itself and countries all over the world.[1][2][3][4]

In addition, there is an ongoing genocide against Muslims in Gaza. [https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_genocide)

#### India

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: India")]

Main article: [Violence against Muslims in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violence_against_Muslims_in_India "Violence against Muslims in India")

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/North_East_Delhi_Riots_2020_%281%29.jpg/250px-North_East_Delhi_Riots_2020_%281%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:North_East_Delhi_Riots_2020_(1).jpg)

Muslim homes and businesses burned during the [North East Delhi riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_East_Delhi_riots "North East Delhi riots").[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-412)

[Communalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communalism_(South_Asia) "Communalism (South Asia)") and [communal violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_violence_in_India "Religious violence in India") is a longstanding problem in Indian society, especially between Hindus and Muslims.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0-134) Scholars have observed that in the Hindu–Muslim communal riots in India, it is invariably Muslims who suffer the greatest losses.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0-134) Proportionately more Muslims are killed and more Muslim property is destroyed.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0-134) In 1961, first major riots took place in [Jabalpur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1961_Jabalpur_Riots "1961 Jabalpur Riots"). In 1964 there were riots in [Jamshedpur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamshedpur "Jamshedpur") and [Rourkela](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rourkela "Rourkela"). Major riots took place in [Ranchi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ranchi "Ranchi"), Bihar in 1967 and in [Ahmedabad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmedabad "Ahmedabad"), Gujarat in 1969. In the 1970s and 1980s major communal riots took place. In many of these riots nearly 1,000 Muslims were killed. In [1992–93, riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bombay_riots "Bombay riots") took place in Bombay in which 50 Muslims perished. From 1992 to 2003 the Muslim community faced a series of communal riots, among which the most serious was the [Babri mosque incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demolition_of_the_Babri_Masjid "Demolition of the Babri Masjid").[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:0-134)

The [2002 Gujarat riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Gujarat_riots "2002 Gujarat riots") were a series of incidents starting with the [Godhra train burning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Godhra_train_burning "Godhra train burning") and the subsequent [communal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communalism_(South_Asia) "Communalism (South Asia)") violence between [Hindus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindus "Hindus") and Muslims in the Indian state of [Gujarat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gujarat "Gujarat"). On 27 February 2002, a Muslim mob burnt the [Sabarmati Express](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabarmati_Express "Sabarmati Express") train and 58 Hindus including 25 women and 15 children were burnt to death. [Frontline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frontline_(U.S._TV_series) "Frontline (U.S. TV series)") claimed that the blame of train burning was put on Muslims,[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-413) while larger sections of media reported that it was Muslim mob which burnt the train.[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-414)[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-415)[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-India_20082-416) Attacks against Muslims and general communal riots arose on a large scale across the state, in which 790 Muslims and 254 Hindus were ultimately killed; 223 more people were reported missing.[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-20000_254_humans2-417)[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-418) 536 places of worship were damaged: 273 [dargahs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dargah "Dargah"), 241 mosques and 19 temples.[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-religious_structures_destroyed2-419) Muslim-owned businesses suffered the bulk of the damage. 6,000 Muslims and 10,000 Hindus fled their homes. Preventive arrests of 17,947 Hindus and 3,616 Muslims were made. In total, 27,901 Hindus and 7,651 Muslims were arrested.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-home.gujarat.gov.in2-420)[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-421)[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-422)

The [2020 Delhi riots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Delhi_riots "2020 Delhi riots"), which left more than 53 dead and hundreds injured including both Hindus and Muslims,[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-423) were triggered by [protests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citizenship_Amendment_Act_protests "Citizenship Amendment Act protests") against a [citizenship law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Citizenship_(Amendment)_Act,_2019 "Citizenship (Amendment) Act, 2019") seen by many critics as anti-Muslim and part of Prime Minister [Narendra Modi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi")'s [Hindu nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_nationalist "Hindu nationalist") agenda.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-424)[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-425)[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-426)[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-427)[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-428) According to [Ashutosh Varshney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashutosh_Varshney "Ashutosh Varshney"), the director of the Center for Contemporary South Asia at [Brown University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_University "Brown University"), “on the whole, the Delhi riots ... are now beginning to look like a [pogrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pogrom "Pogrom"), à la [Gujarat 2002](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2002_Gujarat_riots "2002 Gujarat riots") and [Delhi 1984](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_anti-Sikh_riots "1984 anti-Sikh riots")”.[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-429) According to Subir Sinha, a senior lecturer at the [SOAS University of London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SOAS_University_of_London "SOAS University of London"), the [north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Delhi "North Delhi") and [northeast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_East_Delhi "North East Delhi") areas of Delhi were a focus of "highly inflammatory speeches from top BJP ministers and politicians" in the run-up to the [Delhi election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Delhi_Legislative_Assembly_election "2020 Delhi Legislative Assembly election"). Sinha continues that "the pent-up anger of BJP supporters" who lost the election in Delhi, effectively took it out on "the Muslim residents of these relatively poor parts of the city".[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-430)

According to [Thomas Blom Hansen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Blom_Hansen "Thomas Blom Hansen"), a [Stanford University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_University "Stanford University") professor, across India "a lot of the violence perpetrated against Muslims these days is actually perpetrated by subsidiaries of the [Hindu nationalist movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_nationalism "Hindu nationalism")". According to Hansen, the police harassment of Muslims in Muslim neighborhoods in the run-up to the Delhi riots is "very well-documented".[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Time-431) According to [Sumantra Bose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumantra_Bose "Sumantra Bose"), a [London School of Economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_School_of_Economics "London School of Economics") professor, since [Narendra Modi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi")'s [reelection in May 2019](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Indian_general_election "2019 Indian general election"), his [government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Modi_ministry "Second Modi ministry") has “moved on to larger-scale, if still localized, state-sanctioned mob violence”.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Time-431) In recent years, anti-Muslim violence in India has increased seriously due to the [Hindutva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindutva "Hindutva") ideology,[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-432) where citizens with other religious beliefs are tolerated but have [second‐class status](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second-class_citizen "Second-class citizen").[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-433)

#### Philippines

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Philippines")]

The Muslim [Moro people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moro_people "Moro people") live in the [Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomous_Region_in_Muslim_Mindanao "Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao") and the southern provinces, remain disadvantaged in terms of employment, social mobility, education, and housing. Muslims in the Philippines are frequently discriminated against in the media as scapegoats or warmongers.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-434) This has established escalating tensions that have contributed to the ongoing conflict between the Philippine government, Christians, and Moro people.[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-435)

There has been an ongoing exodus of Moro ([Tausug](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taus%C5%ABg_people "Tausūg people"), [Samal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samal_people "Samal people"), Islamized [Bajau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajau "Bajau"), [Illanun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illanun "Illanun"), and [Maguindanao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maguindanao_people "Maguindanao people")) to Malaysia ([Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah "Sabah")) and Indonesia ([North Kalimantan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Kalimantan "North Kalimantan")) for the last 30 to 50 years, due to the annexation of their lands by Christian Filipino [militants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Militant "Militant") such as the [Ilaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ilaga "Ilaga"), who were responsible for massacres of Muslim villages from the 1970s to the late 1990s. This has changed the population statistics in both countries to a significant degree, and has caused the gradual displacement of the Moros from their traditional lands.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-436)

#### Sri Lanka

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Sri Lanka")]

See also: [2018 anti-Muslim riots in Sri Lanka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_anti-Muslim_riots_in_Sri_Lanka "2018 anti-Muslim riots in Sri Lanka")

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/CPA_DSC05617_%2814603953826%29.jpg/250px-CPA_DSC05617_%2814603953826%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:CPA_DSC05617_(14603953826).jpg)

Protesters hold placards as they demonstrate against the [anti-Muslim violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_anti-Muslim_riots_in_Sri_Lanka "2014 anti-Muslim riots in Sri Lanka") in Sri Lanka, 17 June 2014.

##### Persecution by Sinhala-Buddhist nationalists

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=48 "Edit section: Persecution by Sinhala-Buddhist nationalists")]

Religious minorities have been subjected to increased persecution and attacks owing to the widespread mono-ethnic [Sinhala Buddhist Nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinhalese_Buddhist_nationalism "Sinhalese Buddhist nationalism") in [Sri Lanka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka "Sri Lanka").[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-437)[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-438)[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-439)[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-440)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] A nationalistic Buddhist group, [Bodu Bala Sena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bodu_Bala_Sena "Bodu Bala Sena") (BBS), is alleged to have been behind attacks on Mosques and Muslims,[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-441)[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-442)[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-443)[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-444)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] as well as having organized a moral unofficial police team to check the activities of [Christian missionaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_missionaries "Christian missionaries") and Muslim influence in daily life.[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-colombotelegraph-445)[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-siasat2-446)[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-BBC1-447) The BBC reported that "Sri Lanka's Muslim minority is being targeted by hardline Buddhists. ... There have also been assaults on churches and Christian pastors but it is the Muslims who are the most concerned."[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-448) The BBS has received criticism and opposition from other Buddhist clergy and politicians. [Mangala Samaraweera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mangala_Samaraweera "Mangala Samaraweera"), a Sri Lankan [Theravada Buddhist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism "Theravada Buddhism") politician who has served as [Minister of Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minister_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Sri_Lanka) "Minister of Foreign Affairs (Sri Lanka)") since 2015, has accused the BBS of being "a representation of 'Taliban' terrorism" and of spreading extremism and communal hatred against Muslims.[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ST170213-449)[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-DFT150213-450) Samaraweera has also alleged that the BBS is secretly funded by the [Ministry of Defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Sri_Lanka) "Ministry of Defence (Sri Lanka)").[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ST170213-449)[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-DFT150213-450) Anunayake Bellanwila Wimalaratana, deputy incumbent of [Bellanwila Rajamaha Viharaya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bellanwila_Rajamaha_Viharaya "Bellanwila Rajamaha Viharaya") and President of the Bellanwila Community Development Foundation, has stated that "The views of the Bodu Bala Sena are not the views of the entire [Sangha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sangha_(Buddhism) "Sangha (Buddhism)") community" and that "We don't use our fists to solve problems, we use our brains".[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-451) Wataraka Vijitha Thero, a Buddhist monk who condemns violence against Muslims and heavily criticized the BBS and the government, has been attacked and tortured for his stances.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-452)[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-453)[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-454)[_[check quotation syntax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style#Punctuation "Wikipedia:Manual of Style")_] Sinhala Buddhist Nationalism is opposed to Sarvodaya, although they share many of the same influences like [Dharmapāla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dharmap%C4%81la "Dharmapāla")'s teachings by example, by having a focus upon Sinhalese culture and ethnicity sanctioning the use of violence in defence of dhamma, while Sarvodaya has emphasized the application of Buddhist values in order to transform society and campaigning for peace.[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-455)

##### Persecution by the LTTE

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Persecution by the LTTE")]

Beginning in July 1990, tensions between the [Sri Lankan Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Moors "Sri Lankan Moors") (who constitute a separate ethnic group) and the [Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam "Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam") arose. Tit-for-tat killings between Tamils and Muslims in the [Eastern Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Province,_Sri_Lanka "Eastern Province, Sri Lanka") resulted in the massacres of dozens of Muslims there. This culminated in the infamous [Kattankudy mosque massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kattankudy_mosque_massacre "Kattankudy mosque massacre") in August 1990 by the LTTE.[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-hrw_1991-456) Following these massacres, thousands of Muslims fled Tamil-majority areas of the Eastern Province and resettled in Muslim-majority areas.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-icg_muslims-457)

#### Tajikistan

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Tajikistan")]

Main article: [Islam in Tajikistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Tajikistan "Islam in Tajikistan")

See also: [Religion in Tajikistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_Tajikistan "Religion in Tajikistan")

Sunni Islam of the [Hanafi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hanafi "Hanafi") school has been officially recognized by the government since 2009.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-458) Tajikistan considers itself a [secular state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_state "Secular state") with a Constitution providing for freedom of religion. The Government has declared two Islamic holidays, [Id Al-Fitr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr "Eid ul-Fitr") and [Idi Qurbon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_al-Adha "Eid al-Adha"), as State holidays. According to a [U.S. State Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._State_Department "U.S. State Department") release and Pew research group, the population of Tajikistan is 98% [Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim "Muslim"). The 2012 Pew report stated that approximately 87 of identified as [Sunni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni_Islam "Sunni Islam"), roughly 3% as [Shia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia "Shia") and roughly 7% as [non-denominational Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims "Non-denominational Muslims").[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-459)[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-460) The remaining 2% of the population are followers of [Russian Orthodoxy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church "Russian Orthodox Church"), a variety of Protestant denominations, Catholicism, [Zoroastrianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism "Zoroastrianism"), and Buddhism.

A great majority of Muslims fast during Ramadan, although only about one third in the countryside and 10% in the cities observe daily prayer and dietary restrictions.

There is some reported concern among mainstream Muslim leaders that minority religious groups undermine national unity.[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-461) There is a concern for religious institutions becoming active in the political sphere. The [Islamic Renaissance Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Renaissance_Party_of_Tajikistan "Islamic Renaissance Party of Tajikistan") (IRP), a major combatant in the [1992–1997 Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tajikistan_Civil_War "Tajikistan Civil War") and then-proponent of the creation of an [Islamic state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_religion#Islamic_states "State religion") in Tajikistan, constitutes no more than 30% of the government by statute. Numbers of large mosques appropriate for Friday prayers are limited and some[_[who?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style/Words\_to\_watch#Unsupported\_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")_] feel this is discriminatory.

By law, religious communities must register by the State Committee on Religious Affairs (SCRA) and with local authorities. Registration with the SCRA requires a charter, a list of 10 or more members, and evidence of local government approval prayer site location. Religious groups who do not have a physical structure are not allowed to gather publicly for prayer. Failure to register can result in large fines and closure of place of worship. There are reports that registration on the local level is sometimes difficult to obtain.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-462) People under the age of 18 are also barred from public religious practice.[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-463)

The reason for having Tajikistan in this article is primarily because the government of the country itself, is – or is seen to be – the source of claimed persecution of Muslims. (As opposed to coming from outside forces or other religious groups.) This can make the reported issues open to bias by media and personal religious beliefs or preferences. In fact, the government – with the apparent approval of the people – is attempting to keep the government completely secular (full separation of Church and State) to avoid what they perceive as problems in other surrounding countries.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)

*   The Constitution provides for freedom of religion, and the Government generally respects this right.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   There are some restrictions, and the Government monitors the activities of religious institutions to keep them from becoming overtly political.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   Religious communities must be registered by the Committee on Religious Affairs, which monitors the activities of Muslim groups[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   The official reason given to justify registration is to ensure that religious groups act in accordance with the law but in practice it ensures they do not become overly political.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   President Imomali Rahmonov strongly defended "secularism", likely understood both by the President and his audience, as being "antireligious" rather than "nonreligious."[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   The vast majority of citizens, including members of the Government, consider themselves Muslims and are not anti-Islamic but there is a pervasive fear of Islamic fundamentalism in both the government and much of the population at large.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   A 1998 law prohibits the creation of political parties with a religious orientation.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-U.S._Department_of_State-464)
*   A November 2015 rule reportedly bans Government Employees from attending Friday Prayers.[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-465)[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-eurasianet1-466)
*   The Friday "Government Employee Prayer ban" appears to relate to leaving work during normal working hours to attend prayers. "Over the last two weeks, after Idi Qurbon, our management forbade us from leaving work to attend Friday prayers," one unnamed government employee told Asia-Plus.[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-eurasianet1-466)

Mosques are not permitted to allow women inside due to a fatwa issued in August 2004, by the Tajik Council of Ulema, or scholars – the country's highest Muslim body.[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-467) Part of the reasoning for this is that Tajikistan has 3,980 mosques, but very few are designed to allow men and women to worship separately, a practice Islam generally requires. The fatwa was not strictly enforced and more recently, it has been reported that the Ulema Council will relax the ban.[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-468)

Only state controlled religious education is approved for children and long beards are banned in Tajikistan.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-469)

In Tajikistan, Mosques are banned from allowing Friday Prayers for children younger than 18 year old.[[470]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-470)[[471]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-471)[[472]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-472)[[473]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-473)[[474]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-474)

From the beginning of 2011, 1,500 mosques were shut down by the Tajik government, in addition to banning the hijab for children, banning the use of loudspeakers for the call of prayer, forbidding mosques from allowing women to enter, and monitoring Imams and students learning an Islamic education abroad, having sermons in the Mosque approved by the government and limiting the Mosque sermons to 15 minutes.[[475]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-475) Muslims experienced the most negative effects from the "Religion Law" enacted by the government of Tajikistan, curtailing sermons by Imams during weddings, making the "Cathedral mosques" the only legal place for sermons to be given by Imams with sermons not being allowed in five-fold mosques, the five-fold mosques are small mosques and serve a limited number of people while the medium and big mosques are categorized as Cathedral mosques, girls who wore the hijab have been expelled from schools and hijabs and beards are not permitted on passport photos.[[476]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-476) Mosques have been demolished and shut down by the Tajikistan government on the justification that they were not registered and therefore not considered as mosques by the government.[[477]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-477)[[478]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-478)

Tajikistan has targeted religious groups like Jehovah's Witnesses, Jews, Christians, and Muslims who try to evade control by the government, synagogue, churches, and Mosques have been shut down and destroyed, only a certain amount of mosques are allowed to operate and the state must approve all "religious activity", in which younger than 18-year-old children are not allowed to join in.[[479]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-479) Buildings for religious worship for Jehovah's Witnesses, Protestant Churches, the Jewish Synagogue, and Muslim mosques have been targeted, destroyed, and shut down and prayers are forbidden to take place in public halls, with severed restrictions placed on religion.[[480]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-480) Churches, a synagogue, and mosques have been destroyed by the Tajikistan government.[[481]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-481)

Government approval is required for Tajiks seeking to engage in religious studies in foreign countries and religious activities of Muslims in particular are subjected to controls by the Tajikistan government.[[482]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-482) State control has been implemented on Islamic madrasahs, Imams, and Mosques by Tajikistan.[[483]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-483) A list of sermon "topics" for Imams has been created by the Tajikistan government.[[484]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-484) Towns are only allowed to have a certain number of mosques and only religious buildings sanctioned by the government are allowed to host religious activities, schools have banned hijab, religious studies in private have been forbidden mosque religious services are not allowed to admit children and non-registered mosques have been closed.[[485]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-House2014-485)[[486]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-486)[[487]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-487) Religious matters are banned for children under 18 year old. Public buildings do not allow beards, schools ban hijabs, unregistered mosques are shut down, and sermons are subjected to government authority.[[488]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-488) Only if "provided the child expresses a desire to learn" can a family teach religion to their own children, while the Tajik government banned all non-family private education.[[489]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Lenz-Raymann2014-489) Islam and Muslims have been subjected to controls by the Tajikistan government, the states decides what sermons the Imams give, the government discharges the salaries of Imams and there is only a single madrasah in Tajikistan.[[490]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-490)

Jehovah's Witnesses have been declared illegal in Tajikistan.[[491]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-491) Abundant Life Christian Centre, Ehyo Protestant Church, and Jehovah's witnesses have accused Tajikistan of lying about them not being declared illegal at a Warsaw OSCE conference for human rights.[[492]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-492)

Among increasingly religious Tajiks, Islamic-Arabic names have become more popular over Tajik names.[[493]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-493) However the government has considered the outlawing of Arabic-Islamic names for children.[[494]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-494)[[495]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-495)[[496]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-496)[[497]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-497)[[498]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-498)[[499]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-499)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Tajikistan President Rakhmon (Rahmon) has said that the Persian epic Shahnameh should be used as a source for names, with his proposed law hinting that Muslim names would be forbidden after his anti-hijab and anti-beard laws.[[500]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto1-500)

The Tajik government has used the word "prostitute" to label hijab wearing women and enforced shaving of beards.[[500]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto1-500) As well as that the black coloured Islamic veil was attacked and criticized in public by Tajik President [Emomali Rahmon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon "Emomali Rahmon").[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto-211)

The Islamic Renaissance Party of Tajikistan has been banned by the Tajik government.[[501]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-501)[[502]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-502)[[503]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-503)

Tajikistan's restrictions on Islam has resulted in a drastic decrease of big beards and hijabs.[[504]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-504) Tajikistan bans Salafism under the name "Wahhabi", which is applied to forms of Islam not permitted by the government.[[505]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-505)

160 Islamic clothing stores were shut down and 13,000 men were forcibly shaved by the Tajik police and Arabic names were banned by the parliament of Tajikistan as part of a secularist campaign by President Emomali Rajmon.[[506]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-506)[[507]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-507)[[508]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-508)[[509]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-509)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

Arabic names were outlawed by the legislature of Tajikistan.[[510]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-510)

In Uzbekistan and Tajikistan women wore veils which covered their entire face and body like the [Paranja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paranja "Paranja") and faranji. The traditional veil in Central Asia worn before modern times was the faranji but it was banned by the Soviet Communists[[511]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-AbdullaevAkbarzaheh2010-511) but the Tajikistan President Emomali has misleadingly tried to claim that veils were not part of Tajik culture.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto-211)

After an Islamic Renaissance Party member was allowed to visit Iran by the Iranian government a diplomatic protest was made by Tajikistan.[[512]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-512)

#### Vietnam

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Vietnam")]

The [Cham Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chams "Chams") in Vietnam are only recognized as a minority, and not as an indigenous people by the Vietnamese government despite being indigenous to the region. Muslim Chams have experienced violent religious and ethnic persecution and restrictions on practising their faith under the current Vietnamese government, with the Vietnamese state confisticating Cham property and forbidding Cham from observing their religious beliefs. In 2010 and 2013 several incidents occurred in Thành Tín and Phươc Nhơn villages where Cham were murdered by Vietnamese. In 2012, Vietnamese police in Chau Giang village stormed into a Cham Mosque, stole the electric generator, and also raped Cham girls.[[513]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-513) Cham Muslims in the Mekong Delta have also been economically marginalized and pushed into poverty by Vietnamese policies, with ethnic [Vietnamese Kinh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnamese_people "Vietnamese people") settling on majority Cham land with state support, and religious practices of minorities have been targeted for elimination by the Vietnamese government.[[514]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-514)

### Europe

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=52 "Edit section: Europe")]

#### Bosnia and Herzegovina

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=53 "Edit section: Bosnia and Herzegovina")]

Main articles: [Islam in Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Islam in Bosnia and Herzegovina") and [Bosnian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnian_genocide "Bosnian genocide")

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Bombed_mosque_in_Ahmici.jpg/250px-Bombed_mosque_in_Ahmici.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bombed_mosque_in_Ahmici.jpg)

A mosque demolished by the [Croatian Defence Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croatian_Defence_Council "Croatian Defence Council") in [Ahmići](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmi%C4%87i "Ahmići"), April 1993

The majority of persecutions that have been reported were during the Bosnian War. Primarily, the actions taken by all three factions has led to the [Bosnian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnian_genocide "Bosnian genocide"), which refers to either the genocidal actions that took place at [Srebrenica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srebrenica "Srebrenica") and [Žepa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C5%BDepa "Žepa")[[515]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-iwpr.net-515) which were committed by the [Army of Republika Srpska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska "Army of Republika Srpska") in 1995, or the broader [ethnic cleansing campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_in_the_Bosnian_War "Ethnic cleansing in the Bosnian War") throughout certain areas that were controlled by Republika Srpska[[516]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-516) during the 1992–1995 [Bosnian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "War in Bosnia and Herzegovina").[[517]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-517)

The events in Srebrenica in 1995 included the complete cleansing of more than 8,000 [Bosniak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosniaks "Bosniaks") men and boys, as well as the mass expulsion of another 25,000–30,000 Bosniak civilians, in and around the town of Srebrenica in [Bosnia and Herzegovina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina "Bosnia and Herzegovina"), committed by units of the Army of the Republika Srpska (VRS) under the command of General [Ratko Mladić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87 "Ratko Mladić").[[518]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-518)[[519]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-519)

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg/250px-Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Srebrenica_massacre_memorial_wall_of_names_2009_2.jpg)

Wall of names at the [Srebrenica Genocide Memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srebrenica_Genocide_Memorial "Srebrenica Genocide Memorial")

The [ethnic cleansing campaign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing_in_Bosnia "Ethnic cleansing in Bosnia") that took place throughout areas controlled by the VRS targeted Bosnian Muslims. The ethnic cleansing campaign included unlawful confinement, murder, rape, sexual assault, torture, beating, robbery, and inhumane treatment of civilians; the targeting of political leaders, intellectuals, and professionals; the unlawful deportation and transfer of civilians; the unlawful shelling of civilians; the unlawful appropriation and plunder of real and personal property; the destruction of homes and businesses; and the destruction of places of worship.[[520]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-520)

The [Srebrenica massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srebrenica_massacre "Srebrenica massacre"), also known as the Srebrenica genocide[[521]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-521)[[522]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-522)[[523]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-523)[[524]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-524)[[525]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-IWPR_Oct31-525)[[526]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-526)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] ([Bosnian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnian_language "Bosnian language"): _Genocid u Srebrenici_), was the July 1995 killing of more than 8,000[[527]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-potocarimc.ba-527)[[528]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-528)[[529]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-529)[[530]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-530)[[531]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-531)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_][Bosniaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosniaks "Bosniaks") (Bosnian Muslims), mainly men and boys, in and around the town of Srebrenica during the [Bosnian War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bosnian_War "Bosnian War"). The killing was perpetrated by units of the [Army of Republika Srpska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_of_Republika_Srpska "Army of Republika Srpska") (VRS) [under the command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command_responsibility "Command responsibility") of General [Ratko Mladić](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ratko_Mladi%C4%87 "Ratko Mladić"). The Secretary-General of the United Nations described the [mass murder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_murder "Mass murder") as the worst crime on European soil since the Second World War.[[532]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-532)[[533]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-UN_SecGen_10th_anniv-533) A paramilitary unit from [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Serbia_(1990%E2%80%932006) "Republic of Serbia (1990–2006)") known as the [Scorpions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scorpions_(paramilitary) "Scorpions (paramilitary)"), officially part of the Serbian Interior Ministry until 1991, participated in the massacre,[[534]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Williams-534)[[535]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ReferenceC-535) along with several hundred Russian and [Greek volunteers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Volunteer_Guard "Greek Volunteer Guard").[[536]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-536)[[537]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-537)

#### Bulgaria

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=54 "Edit section: Bulgaria")]

In 1989, 310,000 Turks left Bulgaria, many of them left under pressure as a result of the communist dictator [Todor Zhivkov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Todor_Zhivkov "Todor Zhivkov") regime's assimilation campaign (though up to a third of them returned before the end of the year). That program, which began in 1984, forced all Turks and all other Muslims who lived in Bulgaria to adopt [Bulgarian names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgarian_name "Bulgarian name") and renounce all Muslim customs. The motivation behind the 1984 assimilation campaign is unclear; however, some experts believe that the disproportionately high birth rate of the Turks and the lower birth rate of the Bulgarians were major factors.[[538]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-autogenerated1-538) During the name-changing phase of the campaign, Turkish towns and villages were surrounded by army units. Citizens were issued new identity cards with Bulgarian names. Failure to present a new card meant forfeiture of salary, pension payments, and bank withdrawals. Birth or marriage certificates would only be issued in Bulgarian names. Traditional Turkish costumes were banned; homes were searched and all signs of Turkish identity were removed. Mosques were closed. According to contemporary estimates, 500 to 1,500 people were killed when they resisted assimilation measures, and thousands of others were imprisoned, sent to labour camps or forcibly resettled.[[539]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-539)

#### France

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=55 "Edit section: France")]

In the week after the Islamist terrorist attack against _[Charlie Hebdo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie\_Hebdo "Charlie Hebdo")_ which made 23 casualties, 54 anti-Muslim incidents were reported in France. These included 21 reports of actions (shootings with non-lethal weapons such as bb gun and dummy grenades) against Islamic buildings (e.g. mosques) and 33 cases of threats and insults.[[540]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-540)[[541]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-541)[[542]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-542)[[543]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-543)[[544]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-544)[[545]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-545)[[546]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-546)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Three grenades were thrown at a mosque in Le Mans, west of Paris, and a bullet hole was found in its windows.[[547]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-547) A Muslim prayer hall in the Port-la-Nouvelle was also fired at. There was an explosion at a restaurant affiliated to a mosque in Villefranche-sur-Saône. No casualties were reported.[[548]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-548) Seven days after the attack, Mohamed El Makouli was stabbed to death at home by 28-year-old neighbour Thomas Gambet shouting "I am your God, I am your Islam." His wife, Nadia, suffered hand injuries while she tried to save him.[[549]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-549)

Between 24 and 28 December 2015, a Muslim prayer hall was burned down and [Qur'ans were set alight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran_desecration "Quran desecration") following marches by Corsican nationalists in a [series of protests in Corsica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Corsican_protests "2015 Corsican protests"). The protesters claimed to be acting in revenge for an incident that occurred the day prior when firefighters and police were assaulted in the neighbourhood of Jardins de l'Empereur;[[550]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-imported-550) however, outside observers labeled the ensuing riots as [anti-Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Arabism "Anti-Arabism") and [anti-Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Muslim_sentiment "Anti-Muslim sentiment"). The Corsican nationalist politicians have claimed their view does not legitimise [xenophobia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xenophobia "Xenophobia"), blaming the protest on [French nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_nationalism "French nationalism") instead.[[550]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-imported-550) Scholarly opinions on this claim are divided.[[551]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ibn-551)

#### Germany

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=56 "Edit section: Germany")]

On 28 May 1993, four [neo-Nazi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Nazism "Neo-Nazism")[skinheads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_power_skinhead "White power skinhead") (ages 16–23) [set fire to the house](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993_Solingen_arson_attack "1993 Solingen arson attack") of a [Muslim Turk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_people "Turkish people") family in [Solingen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solingen "Solingen") in [North Rhine-Westphalia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Rhine-Westphalia "North Rhine-Westphalia"). As a result of the attack 3 girls and 2 women died and 14 other family members, including several children, were injured, some of them severely.[[552]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-rally-552)[[553]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-zeit-553)

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Brandanschlag_solingen_1993.jpg/250px-Brandanschlag_solingen_1993.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brandanschlag_solingen_1993.jpg)

Common demonstration of Germans and Turks at the site of the [Solingen arson attack of 1993](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solingen_arson_attack_of_1993 "Solingen arson attack of 1993")

On 9 June 2004 a [nail bombing in a business area popular with Turkish immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Cologne_bombing "2004 Cologne bombing") in [Cologne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cologne "Cologne") injured 22 Turks, completely destroyed a barber shop and many other shops and seriously damaged numerous parked cars.[[554]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-554)[[555]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-555)

On 1 July 2009, [Marwa El-Sherbini was stabbed to death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_of_Marwa_El-Sherbini "Murder of Marwa El-Sherbini") in a courtroom in [Dresden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dresden "Dresden"), Germany. She had just given evidence against her attacker who had used insults against her because she wore an [Islamic headscarf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab "Hijab"). El-Sherbini was called "[Islamist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamism "Islamism")", "terrorist", and (according to one report) "slut".[[note 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-noteoninsults-556)

The [National Socialist Underground murders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Socialist_Underground_murders "National Socialist Underground murders") took place between 2000 and 2006. The Neo-Nazi group killed 10 people. The police discovered a hit list of 88 people that included "two prominent members of the Bundestag and representatives of Turkish and Islamic groups".[[556]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-557)

German officials recorded more than 70 attacks against mosques from 2012 to 2014.[[557]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-558) In 2016, 91 mosques in Germany were attacked. Police stated that the majority of cases have gone unsolved, and only one arrest was made so far.[[558]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-559) There were 950 attacks reportedly on Muslims and mosques in Germany in 2017 injuring 34 Muslims.[[559]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-560)[[560]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-561) In 2018, police recorded 813 hate crimes against Muslims, injuring at least 54 Muslims.[[561]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-562) 132 Islamophobic incidents occurred in Germany in the first half of 2019, injuring 4 Muslims.[[562]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-563)

On 17 July 2018, a man fired six shots at a female employee wearing a headscarf in a Turkish-owned bakery, leaving no casualties.[[563]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-564)

#### Netherlands

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=57 "Edit section: Netherlands")]

According to research by Ineke van der Valk, an author and researcher at the University of Amsterdam, a third of mosques in the Netherlands have experienced at least one incident of vandalism, threatening letters, attempted arson, or other aggressive actions in the past 10 years.[[564]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-DutchJaz-565)[[565]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-566)

#### Norway

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=58 "Edit section: Norway")]

On 22 July 2011, [two sequential lone wolf domestic terrorist attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Norway_attacks "2011 Norway attacks") by [Anders Behring Breivik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders_Behring_Breivik "Anders Behring Breivik") against the government, the civilian population, and a [Workers' Youth League (AUF)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_Youth_League_(Norway) "Workers' Youth League (Norway)") summer camp killed 77 people and injured at least 319.[[566]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-formell-tiltale-567)[[567]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-helsedir-rapport-568)[[568]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ems-response2-569)[[569]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-dtoll-names-570)[[570]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-dtoll-all-names-published-571)[[571]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-died-from-wounds-572)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] Analysts described him as having [Islamophobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobic "Islamophobic") views and a hatred of Islam,[[572]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-573)[[573]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-574) and as someone who considered himself as a knight dedicated to stemming the tide of Muslim immigration into Europe.[[574]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-575)[[575]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-576) In a [manifesto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifesto "Manifesto"), he describes opposition to what he saw as the Islamisation of Europe as his motive for carrying out the attacks.[[576]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Goodman-577)

On 10 August 2019 21 year old lone gunman [Philip Manshaus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philip_Manshaus "Philip Manshaus")[opened fire on a mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A6rum_mosque_shooting "Bærum mosque shooting") in [Bærum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B%C3%A6rum "Bærum"), Norway, a suburbia 20 kilometers outside of Oslo. He injured one person and was then subdued by two worshippers. At the time of the shooting there were three congregants in the mosque.[[577]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-578)[[578]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-579)[[579]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-580)

#### Sweden

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=59 "Edit section: Sweden")]

Two people died and 13 were injured in [a series of shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Malm%C3%B6_shootings "2009–10 Malmö shootings") targeting people with dark skin and non-Swedish appearance in [Malmö](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malm%C3%B6 "Malmö") in 2009 and 2010. The perpetrator had "strong anti-immigrant sentiments" and all but one of the victims were not ethnically Swedish.[[580]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-581)[[581]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-BBC2-582)[[582]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Nyberg-583)[[583]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-584)[[584]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-585)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

Between 25 December 2014 and 1 January 2015, three arson attack against mosques occurred across Sweden in [Eslöv](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esl%C3%B6v "Eslöv"), [Uppsala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uppsala "Uppsala") and [Eskilstuna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eskilstuna "Eskilstuna") injuring at least five Muslim civilians.[[585]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Euronews2-586)[[586]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Local3-587)[[587]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-sverigesradio3-588)[[588]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Guardian2-589)[[589]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Newsweek2-590)[[590]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Local22-591)[[591]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-592)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

On 22 October 2015, [a masked swordsman killed three and wounded another at Kronan School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trollh%C3%A4ttan_school_attack "Trollhättan school attack") in [Trollhättan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trollh%C3%A4ttan "Trollhättan"). The perpetrator chose the school as his target due to its high immigrant population. He was later shot and killed by police. It is the deadliest attack on a school in Swedish history.[[592]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-593)[[593]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-594)

#### Switzerland

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=60 "Edit section: Switzerland")]

[Zürich Islamic center shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich_Islamic_center_shooting "Zürich Islamic center shooting") was a [mass shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_shooting "Mass shooting") of several people in an [Islamic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") center in Central [Zürich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich "Zürich") that occurred on 19 December 2016. Three people were wounded in the attack, two seriously, though all are expected to survive.[[594]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-SwissInfo-595)[[595]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-theguardianthreeinjured-596)[[596]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-bbcswissshooting-597)[[597]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-598)[[598]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-ICC-599)[[599]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-NYTimes-600)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_]

In 2019, one in every two Muslims in Switzerland stated that they had been discriminated against based on their religious identity.[[600]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:3-601)

#### United Kingdom

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=61 "Edit section: United Kingdom")]

In 2015, 46% of Muslims in United Kingdom stated that they think being Muslim in U.K. is difficult.[[601]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-602)

In 2016, 1,223 cases of Islamophobic attacks were reported to Tell MAMA.[[602]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-setav.org-603)

After the [Manchester Arena bombing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manchester_Arena_bombing "Manchester Arena bombing") in May 2017, there was a 700% rise in the number of reported [hate crimes against Muslims in the U.K.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobia_in_the_United_Kingdom#Hate_crimes "Islamophobia in the United Kingdom")[[603]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:4-604)[_[unreliable source](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable\_sources "Wikipedia:Reliable sources")_] 94,098 hate crimes were recorded in the country in 2017–2018, 52% of them targeted Muslims which is about 130 to 140 hate crimes against Muslims reported each day. [Scotland Yard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scotland_Yard "Scotland Yard") stated that such crimes were "hugely underreported".[[604]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-firstpost.com-605) According to [Tell MAMA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tell_MAMA "Tell MAMA"), between March and July 2017, 110 attacks targeting mosques occurred in United Kingdom.

[Boris Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boris_Johnson "Boris Johnson")'s comments on women wearing the veil in August 2018 led to a surge in anti-Muslim attacks and incidents of abuse. In the week following Johnson's comments, Tell MAMA said anti-Muslim incidents increased from eight incidents the previous week, to 38 in the following which equals an increase of 375%. Twenty-two of the recorded anti-Muslim hate crimes targeted women who wore the niqab, or face veil.[[604]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-firstpost.com-605)

In 2019, there were 3,530 recorded cases of Islamophobic hate crime in UK.[[600]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:3-601) A week after the March 2019 [Christchurch mosque shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christchurch_mosque_shootings "Christchurch mosque shootings") in New Zealand, the number of reported hate crimes against Muslims increased by 593% and 95 incidents were reported to The Guardian between 15 March (day of the [Christchurch mosque shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christchurch_mosque_shootings "Christchurch mosque shootings")) and midnight on 21 March.[[603]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:4-604)[[605]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-606)

In April 2025, up to 100 graves, including those of Muslim children and babies, were vandalised in a Muslim section of the Carpenders Park Lawn cemetery in Watford, United Kingdom. Apparently, grave markers had been uprooted and scattered across the grass. Police are investigating the incident as an Islamophobic hate crime and have appealed for witnesses and further information from the public. Brent Council, which owns the cemetery, has promised to reinstate the damaged name plaques once the police investigation is complete. The Muslim community has been profoundly shocked by the desecration, with Saqib Nadeem, president of the Ahmadiyya Muslim Association Watford, describing the vandalism as "heartbreaking."[[606]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-607)

### North America

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=62 "Edit section: North America")]

#### Canada

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=63 "Edit section: Canada")]

[Police forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Canada "Law enforcement in Canada") from across Canada have reported that Muslims are the second most targeted religious group, after Jews. And while hate crimes against all religious groups (except Jews) have decreased, hate crimes against Muslims have increased following 9/11.[[607]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-608)[[608]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Paperny-609)[[609]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:2-610)[[610]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-611)[_[excessive citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources#Bundling\_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] In 2014, police forces recorded 99 religiously motivated [hate crimes against Muslims in Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobia_in_Canada#Hate_crimes "Islamophobia in Canada"), the number was 45 in 2012.[[609]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-:2-610)

In 2015, the city of [Toronto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toronto "Toronto") reported a similar trend: hate crimes in general decreased by 8.2%, but hate crimes against Muslims had increased.[[611]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-TorontoSpike-612) Police hypothesized the spike could be due to the [Paris attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/November_2015_Paris_attacks "November 2015 Paris attacks") or anger over refugees. Muslims faced the third highest level of hate crimes in Toronto, after Jews and the LGBTQ community.[[611]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-TorontoSpike-612)

On 29 January 2017, a [mass shooting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_shooting "Mass shooting") occurred at the [Islamic Cultural Centre of Quebec City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Cultural_Centre_of_Quebec_City "Islamic Cultural Centre of Quebec City"), killing 6 and injuring 19 Muslims. Prime Minister [Justin Trudeau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_Trudeau "Justin Trudeau") and Premier [Philippe Couillard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippe_Couillard "Philippe Couillard") called the shooting a [terrorist attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorist_attack "Terrorist attack"),[[612]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Kassam_and_Lartey-613)[[613]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-auto2-614) but the perpetrator was not charged with terrorism.[[614]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-WhyNoTerrorism-615) The incident was classified as a [hate crime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_crime "Hate crime")[[615]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Washington_Post_shooting_2017-616) and an [Islamophobic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobic "Islamophobic") attack.[[616]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Al-Jazeera-617)

In June 2021, five members of a Muslim family were the victims of a [domestic terrorist attack in the city of London, Ontario](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London,_Ontario_truck_attack "London, Ontario truck attack"). Four members died as a result of this attack, leaving the fifth, a 9-year-old boy, with severe injuries.[[617]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-618) The act was reported as premeditated and motivated by anti-Muslim hate.[[618]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-619)

#### United States

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Persecution_of_Muslims&action=edit&section=64 "Edit section: United States")]

See also: [Islamophobia in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamophobia_in_the_United_States "Islamophobia in the United States"), [Anti-Iranian sentiment §United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Iranian_sentiment#United_States "Anti-Iranian sentiment"), and [Stereotypes of Arabs and Muslims in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stereotypes_of_Arabs_and_Muslims_in_the_United_States "Stereotypes of Arabs and Muslims in the United States")

In the [aftermath of 9/11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_September_11_attacks "Aftermath of the September 11 attacks"), the number of [hate crimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hate_crime "Hate crime") against [people of Middle-Eastern descent in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Eastern_Americans "Middle Eastern Americans") increased from 354 attacks in 2000 to 1,501 attacks in 2001.[[619]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-Oswald-620)

Zohreh Assemi, an [Iranian American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Americans "Iranian Americans") Muslim owner of a nail salon in [Locust Valley, New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Locust_Valley,_New_York "Locust Valley, New York"), was robbed, beaten, and called a "terrorist" in September 2007 in what authorities call a bias crime.[[620]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-nypost-621) Assemi was kicked, sliced with a boxcutter, and had her hand smashed with a hammer. The perpetrators, who forcibly removed $2,000 from the salon and scrawled anti-Muslim slurs on the mirrors, also told Assemi to "get out of town" and that her kind were not "welcomed" in the area. The attack followed two weeks of phone calls in which she was called a "terrorist" and told to "get out of town", friends and family said.[[620]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-nypost-621)

On 25 August 2010, a New York taxi driver was stabbed after a passenger asked him whether he was a Muslim.[[621]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-622)

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Abu_Ghraib_53.jpg/250px-Abu_Ghraib_53.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Abu_Ghraib_53.jpg)

[Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Ghraib_torture_and_prisoner_abuse "Abu Ghraib torture and prisoner abuse")

On 27 December 2012, in New York City 31-year-old Erika Menendez allegedly pushed an Indian immigrant and small businessman named Sunando Sen onto the subway tracks where he was struck and killed by a train. Menendez, who has a long history of mental illness[[622]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-623)[[623]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-624) and violence,[[624]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persecution_of_Muslims#cite_note-625) told police: "I pushed a Muslim off the train tracks because I hate Hindus and Muslims... Ever since 2001 when they put down the Twin Towers, I've been beating them up."
